Sun Dianying Has Indeed Left the Army

Subordinate Officers Rebel One After Another, The Situation Is Over

Sun Leaves the Army to Dengkou, Accompanied by Fu Zhankui to Ping

Remnants Monitored by Troops Dispatched by Fu and Ma, Awaiting Reorganization

The Military Campaign Against Sun Can Be Declared Complete

(Beiping) Fu Zhankui's 23rd Telegram to Ping reports that Sun Dianying arrived in Dengkou at 5 PM on the 22nd, preparing to go to Ping with him on the 23rd. After receiving the telegram, He Yingqin immediately telegraphed to Fu Zuoyi, saying that if Sun left the army to go to Ping, he could be allowed to pass through the defense area of the Jin-Sui Army. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Beiping) After the Jin-Sui Army occupied Dengkou, they coordinated with the Ning Army to attack Sun's troops from both sides. Ding Futing, Lü Cunyi, Lu Fengnian, and other units within Sun's army rebelled one after another. Because Sun was unable to fight, and suing for peace would mean losing credibility, he led a part of his guards on the 20th, forcefully collaborating with Zhuan Sunziyu's brigade to attack Pingluo, intending to use it as a base. However, because the Ma army in the city held firm, Sun knew that the matter could not be accomplished. That night, he left the army. After Sun left the army, his remnants were temporarily monitored by troops dispatched by Fu and Ma, awaiting orders for reorganization. The Jin-Sui Army and Ning Army units are still advancing towards Pingluo. The military campaign against Sun can be declared complete in the coming days. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Beiping) He Yingqin received a telegram from Men Bingyue this morning, stating that Sun Dianying had left the army on the 20th due to the disintegration of his troops, and his whereabouts were unknown. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Beiping) Sun Dianying telegraphed on the 20th, saying that after Kuiyuan left his post, the Yu, Liu, and Ding units under his command had complied with the Beiping Military Branch Council's order of the 5th. The Yu unit moved to the Hedong area of Ningxia, the Ding unit moved to the area near Ningxia, and the Liu unit moved to the western Sui area, awaiting review. Kuiyuan left the troops on the 17th and arrived in Dengkou on the 20th, accompanying the Fu and Li representatives of the Military Branch Council, and would go to Ping immediately. At this time of national crisis, he would serve the country as a citizen in the future. Respectfully telegraphed for your consideration. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Tianjin) Sui telegram, Fu Zhankui telegraphed Ping early on the 23rd, reporting that Sun Dianying had indeed left the army and gone into retirement, and was currently in Dengkou, preparing to come east together. Most of Sun's troops collapsed and fled north of Dengkou. The siege of Pingluo has been lifted. The Second Brigade of Ma Hongkui's troops occupied Shizuishan, and Zhao Chengzhou's cavalry was pursuing them. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Beiping) Linhe telegram, Wang Jingguo and Zhao Chengzhou arrived in Dengkou at noon on the 21st to supervise and urge the various units to actively advance. The Lü cavalry brigade would reach the vicinity of Shizuishan at noon on the 22nd. The Wang Tingying infantry brigade passed Dengkou at Chenshi (7-9 AM) on the 22nd, marching at full speed towards Shizuishan. Sun Changsheng, Tian Shumei, Jin Zhonghe, and other brigades were also advancing one after another, aiming to actively pressure Sun's troops and resolve the situation as soon as possible. Lu Fengnian immediately rebelled and obeyed the central government. In this way, the Jin-Sui Army's occupation of Shizuishan would not lead to a major battle. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Beiping) Ningxia telegram, a brigade of Ning Army cavalry and the Zhao Chengzhou cavalry of the Jin-Sui Army jointly occupied Shizuishan on the afternoon of the 22nd. The remnants of Sun's troops collapsed and retreated north of Dengkou. Sun himself arrived in Dengkou last night. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Beiping) Ma Hongkui occupied Shizuishan yesterday, and the siege of Pingluo has been lifted. Seeing that the situation was over, Sun arrived in Dengkou yesterday afternoon and met with Fu, looking dejected. He intended to leave the army to go to Ping with Fu. He also dispatched staff officer Tao Jun from Ping this afternoon to Sui to work with Men Bingyue and Fu Zuoyi to handle the aftermath of Sun's army. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Beiping) Men Bingyue telegraphed Ping, saying that Sun expressed his willingness to leave the army, but the aftermath of his troops had not yet been negotiated. Therefore, he asked Fu to stay in Shizuishan for a few more days to discuss everything. After the arrangements were completed, Fu would return east, and Sun would go to Jin to stay for a while. Sun's troops under Yu Shiming would be transferred to Hedong in Ningxia, Liu Yueting's troops would be transferred to western Sui, and Ding Futing's troops would be transferred between Ningxia and Pingluo, awaiting reorganization. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Beiping) Lu Fengnian sent a cipher telegram to Ping last night, declaring his obedience to the central government. Whether his troops were reorganized or reduced, he was willing to obey orders. At the same time, he telegraphed Yan Xishan, Zhu Shaoliang, and Ma Hongkui to report, and telegraphed Sun, advising him to rein in at the edge of the cliff and avoid future regrets. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Beiping) Sun owes money to the Baotou-Linhe area. After Fu was ordered by the Military Branch Council to investigate, he telegraphed Ping to confirm the facts. Sun intends to request the Military Branch Council to allocate the repayment from the three months of arrears in the troops' pay. However, the authorities have already allocated this money to the Jin-Sui Army for use. Since Sun has expressed his intention to leave the army, a meeting should be convened to discuss the repayment method. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Beiping) Linhe telegram, on the evening of the 18th, Sun's troops were still attacking Pingluo with all their might, and the situation was quite critical. The Ma Brigade Commander defending Pingluo telegraphed for help. The original telegram stated that the enemy troops used fierce artillery fire to attack our Yuhuang Pavilion and the northwest corner of the city at 7 PM, and our Ma and Yu battalion commanders were injured, with dozens of soldiers and many civilians killed and wounded. Please advance troops quickly in order to encircle and lift the siege of Pingluo. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Beiping) After Fu arrived in Baotou and Linhe, he sent personnel to the families of the military officers stationed in the Baotou-Linhe area to convey the Military Branch Council's great intention of not investigating the past actions of Sun's military officers and providing them with preferential arrangements. The officers of Sun's army received reports from their families, so they sent representatives to Linhe to discuss surrendering (23rd telegram).

(Beiping) Regarding Sun personally, the authorities have always adopted a lenient approach, hoping that Sun can come to live in Ping, and everything can still be absolutely guaranteed. The authorities also telegraphed this intention to Fu. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Beiping) A certain military officer said that the Jin-Sui Army's advance this time was greatly aided by the strength of Lu Fengnian's division. At the same time, because Sun's main force was divided to besiege Ningyuan and Pingluo, the troops were dispersed, and the siege had been going on for a long time, the soldiers' morale was flagging, so the progress could be so rapid. The Ningxia Ma Hongkui troops, in collaboration with the □ brigade of Hu Zongnan's division, began their northern attack at dawn on the 19th, and it went quite smoothly. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Beiping) News from the military that Lu Fengnian, the commander of Sun's 119th Division, had led his troops to rebel, had recently telegraphed the Military Branch Council, stating that Fengnian was a mere soldier and had long seen the disaster of internal strife that could not be allowed to rise again. Since receiving the central government's order on February 5th, he had intended to comply, so that the locality could be stabilized as soon as possible. However, he hoped that Military Commander Dianying could repent, and the entire army should take a unified attitude, which should not be expressed. Unexpectedly, even today, Military Commander Dianying still held his own views, so he had no choice but to take decisive action. On the 23rd, he led his troops to obey the central government, unable to harm the greater good for small matters, or abandon public benefit for private friendship. Whether this is appropriate, please issue clear instructions on the direction, etc. (23rd Central News Agency Telegram)

Han Fuqu Vigorously Suppresses Bandit Liu

Liu is Surrounded by a Large Force at Daokou Pass, Northwest of Jieshou

Han and Sun Tongxuan Personally Supervise the Troops

(Jinan) Tonight, bandit Liu was surrounded by a large force at Daokou Pass, more than 60 li northwest of Jieshou in Changqing County. Han and Division Commander Sun Tongxuan, Brigade Commander Yun Qichang, have all arrived in Jieshou to supervise the troops and are vigorously suppressing them. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Jinan) Han mobilized troops to block the bandits at the four stations of Jieshou, Zhangxia, Gushan, and Wand, Sun Tongxuan went to Tai today to meet with Han. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Jinan) Bandit Liu burned more than ten villages in Yuncheng and Wenshang, and massacred more than eighty people in Juye. Many of bandit Liu's troops have dispersed, and dozens have been captured in Jinan, Ningyang, and Yanzhou. (22nd Special Telegram)

(Jinan) Today's official news: Bandit Liu's remnants who fled to Feicheng are currently being pursued by Wangjiazhuang and Shi Tuanzheng, 25 li from the city. Those who fled to Dongping are also being pursued by Gu Liangyou and Xie Shuxian's militia at Shahe Station. The cavalry regiment under Li Xuande advanced from Anjiazhuang last night. Feng pays great attention to bandit disturbances. Peng Guozheng, the commander of Feng's guard regiment, captured a mortar and dozens of prisoners while suppressing Liu in Anjiazhuang on the 22nd. Liu begged Han for leniency, willing to be reorganized. Han resolutely refused and is determined to suppress him to the end, eliminating the scourge for several provinces in North China. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Beiping) Jiang Bocheng will go to Jinan tomorrow morning (23rd telegram).

Observations on the Situation in North China Amidst Rumors

No Changes Expected for the Time Being

(Beiping) Regarding the situation in North China, there have been widespread rumors in the outside world in the past week that it is becoming tense again. According to sources concerned, the Japanese have now canceled special expenses for North China, and the units along the Great Wall have also returned to their normal state. The 10th and 14th Divisions in northern Manchuria have been ordered to be transferred back to their country, and the new replacement troops have not yet arrived. At the same time, the Japanese army is currently concentrating near cities with regiments as military units, actively training. In this way, no changes are expected for the time being. Although the Japanese army has increased troops in eastern Chahar, the problem in Chahar Province is also the entire problem of North China. If there are no plans for the entire North China for the time being, then no major problems are expected in Chahar Province at present. (23rd Special Telegram)

Japanese Plan to Divide Pseudo-Army Forces by Military Region

(Beiping) After the Japanese ordered the cancellation of the garrison commands in various places in the Northeast, they have decided to start planning seven major military regions from April 1st, and limit the pseudo-army to be concentrated in each military region before July 1st. The Japanese are doing this purely to divide the pseudo-army forces, so that they will never rebel, and will take the opportunity to resolve them. (23rd Special Telegram)

Eastern Route Headquarters Moves from Xiamen to Zhangzhou

Jiang Dingwen Bids Farewell to All Circles in Xiamen

The 9th Division Completes its Departure for Western Fujian

(Xiamen) The Eastern Route Headquarters is scheduled to move from Xiamen to Zhangzhou on the 24th. The Office, the General Staff Office, and the Adjutant's Office will depart first on the morning of the 24th. All remaining party, government, military, legal, medical, and secretarial staff will follow. Jiang Dingwen will go to Zhangzhou on the 25th. The headquarters will be located at the Zhangzhou Minnan Hospital. Only an office will be left in Xiamen. Jiang is scheduled to bid farewell to all circles in Xiamen on the 24th. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Xiamen) The 9th Division's departure for western Fujian can be completed from Zhangzhou on the 24th. According to reports in Hong Kong newspapers, the Communist bandits are attacking Longyan, but there is no news of this from officials or private sources in Zhangzhou and Xiamen. There were still cars carrying military supplies to Longyan on the 23rd. A part of the 3rd Division is currently stationed in Daxiaochi, northwest of Longyan, and a part is stationed in Gutian, northeast of Longyan. The Communist bandit Luo Binghui is in Changting, and a part is in Liancheng. A part of the 83rd Division is stationed in Longyan, and a part is stationed in Shizhong. There is also no news of contact with the main force of the bandits at the front. (23rd Special Telegram)

Fujian Militia Still Undergoing Review

(Fuzhou) The various small militia units are currently continuing to be reviewed. The best of them will be selected and added to the security team in two or three regiments. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Fuzhou) The Fujian Headquarters and the Central Transport Office are scheduled to return to Nanchang one after another on the 24th. The North China Relief Team arrived in Fujian on the 23rd. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Fuzhou) Wei Lihuang is still not fully recovered from his illness and plans to go to Shanghai for medical treatment. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Fuzhou) Li Shijia postponed his trip to Xiamen due to leading the land and water teams to suppress the bandits in Lianluo. (23rd Special Telegram)

He Yingqin Telegraphed His Resignation as Mongolian Autonomous Official

Qinghai Representatives Request Increase in Number of Political Committee Members

(Beiping) He Yingqin is too busy with official duties and has no time to take care of the Mongolian Autonomous Official position. He has telegraphed the central government to resign. The central government has not yet replied. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Nanjing) Zhao Pilian, the vice chairman of the Mongolian Association, visited Director Wang on the 23rd to convey the opinions of the Mongolian people of various leagues and banners in Qinghai and the Tumote Banner, requesting an increase in the number of members of the Mongolian Local Autonomous Political Committee. Wang agreed to telegraph Chairman Jiang for consultation and decision. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Nanjing) The Qinghai representatives in Beijing submitted a request to add the four league leaders and deputy league leaders of the two leagues to the Mongolian Autonomous Political Committee, as well as the case of the Tumote Banner officials and people requesting the appointment of Man Tai as a member. The Mongolian Association has prepared a review opinion and submitted it to the Standing Committee on the 23rd for approval in accordance with the review opinion. (23rd Special Telegram)

(Nanjing) Qinghai representative Yu Jiabao requested that the four ministerial heads of Qinghai Province not included in the list of Mongolian Autonomous Political Affairs Committee members released by the central government, requesting to be appointed to join, and the number of members be changed to 28, etc. The Executive Yuan handed it over to the Mongolian-Tibetan Committee for review. (23rd Special Telegram)

Page 4

No Negotiations Conducted Before or After the Exchange of Notes Between the US and Japan

Japanese Navy Department Insists on Changing the Ratio

US Navy Bill Sent to Roosevelt for Signature

Philippine Independence Bill Passed by US Congress

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs announced that the U.S. State Department sent a telegram to foreign envoys and consuls on the 21st to explain the unofficial exchange of letters between the United States and Japan. A translation is as follows: "The original text of the unofficial letters exchanged between Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota and U.S. Secretary of State Hull has been published in newspapers in Tokyo and Washington. No negotiations whatsoever have been conducted between the two governments prior to this, nor are any negotiations being conducted now." (23rd Central News Agency Telegram)

(Tokyo) Regarding the exchange of documents between Hirota and Hull, the Ministry of the Navy issued the following opinion in the form of a conversation yesterday: "The morning editions of various newspapers on the 21st carried a telegram from London, saying that the empire would satisfy the current naval ratio in exchange for the revision of the anti-Japanese immigration law, recognition of "Manchukuo," and Philippine independence. However, this is contrary to the facts. The Imperial Navy is determined to revise the current naval ratio and has not changed in any way." (23rd Den-tsu Telegram)

(Washington) The Senate passed the 500 million yuan naval expansion appropriation bill today. This bill has now been sent to the President for signature. This bill was passed by the Senate on March 6, but a number of additional clauses were added, which were rejected by the House of Representatives. The bill was returned to the Senate for reconsideration two days ago, and it was passed in its original form today. (22nd Reuters Telegram)

(Washington) The United States' most advantageous naval bill has been passed by both houses of Congress and will be sent to the President for signature today. Congressional action on this bill has come to an end. When the Senate passed the additional clauses, opponents created obstacles to the vote on the committee report, but they were ultimately ineffective. The House of Representatives passed this bill this morning and sent it to the Senate. It is said that President Roosevelt will soon approve this bill, as the President believes that this bill will not only strengthen the United States' national defense but also create jobs for thousands of workers. The Vincent-Trammell Naval Act stipulates that the United States Navy will build 102 warships and 1,184 aircraft. The Senate's amendments to this bill were finally passed by the House of Representatives. The Senate's amendments limit the profits that private companies can make from building warships and aircraft to 10 percent, in order to avoid outsiders from profiting from the naval program. There are no specific regulations for the allocation of funds in this bill, but the funds required for shipbuilding in the future will be approved by Congress at any time. (23rd National Telegram)

(Washington) The Philippine Islands Independence Bill, proposed by Democratic Senator Tydings and Representative McDuffie in reference to the President's message, was passed by the House of Representatives on the 19th of this month and transferred to the Senate. The Senate put it to discussion today, and as a result, it passed with a large majority of 68 votes to 8 votes. Before the vote, a number of amendments were proposed, the most important of which was Senator King's proposal to allow the Philippine Islands to be independent immediately, but it was not passed. According to the Independence Bill passed by the House of Representatives and the Senate before and after, it is stipulated that the Philippines will be completely independent within twelve years, organize a republic, and after the declaration of independence, the U.S. Army stationed in the Philippines should withdraw immediately, while the naval bases will be left to be resolved after independence. (22nd Havas Telegram)

Diplomatic Authorities' Observation on the Exchange of Notes Between the US and Japan

Unlikely to be Recognized as an Organization

(Nanjing) Newspapers reported the exchange of diplomatic documents between the United States and Japan, and officials from various countries are paying close attention to this. A British newspaper even claimed that the United States might recognize the puppet state, etc. As this matter is of great importance to our country, the reporter went to ask a certain diplomatic authority. According to the discussion, the documents exchanged between the United States and Japan are of an informal nature, but since the full text has not yet been seen, there is no way to make an accurate judgment. However, based on observations at this time, the motive for the exchange of notes between the United States and Japan may be to ease the tense atmosphere between the United States and Japan over the past two years, and there is no other effect. This is evidenced by the U.S. State Department's telegram to its embassies abroad, stating that "no negotiations whatsoever have been conducted between the United States and Japan prior to this, nor are any negotiations being conducted now." This kind of observation may not be wrong. As for the claim of not recognizing the puppet organization, the U.S. government has repeatedly declared that it is its consistent policy, and the United States Minister to Switzerland formally replied to the Secretary-General of the League of Nations agreeing to the measures regarding non-recognition of the puppet state passed by the Advisory Committee of the League of Nations on June 7 last year. We firmly believe that the U.S. government will implement its consistent claims and will not recognize the existence of the puppet organization. (23rd Central News Agency Telegram)

Britain Decides Not to Recognize the Puppet Organization

If the Situation Changes, It Must Be Discussed by the League of Nations

(Nanjing) When the reporter met with the British Minister this morning on the 23rd, he inquired about Britain's attitude towards the puppet organization. According to the Minister, Britain is a loyal member state of the League of Nations and will abide by the League's resolutions, will not recognize the puppet Manchukuo, and will not consider this issue. The reporter asked again whether Britain's attitude would change due to changes in the situation. The Minister continued, if the situation changes to the point where the League of Nations must consider the issue of recognition or non-recognition, the British government will also have to consider it. (23rd Central News Agency Telegram)

US-Japan Negotiations Promote the Opening of the Pacific Conference

Commentary from the French Press

(Paris) The French press commented on the Washington negotiations. The French press believes that Japan's purpose is not only to discuss the Far East issue, but also the naval issue will be raised for discussion. When conducting naval negotiations, Japan will definitely demand that the United States recognize "Manchukuo," revise the U.S. immigration law, and abolish the U.S. naval and air bases in the Philippines as exchange conditions. The French side expects that the result of informal direct negotiations will be to promote the early opening of the Pacific Conference, which will be attended by all countries concerned about the Far East issue. (23rd World News Agency Telegram)

The Far East Issue Has Become International in Nature

Commentary from the Manchester Guardian

(London) The Manchester Guardian criticized the exchange of notes between the US and Japan today, saying that Japan's move was caused by the Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov's gaining recognition from the United States. U.S. Secretary of State Hull's statement that all countries related to the Far East have the right to discuss issues with each other is very important, as it is tantamount to registering the international nature of the Far East issue. According to the New York Times' Tokyo dispatch, the Japanese government believes that the future status of the Philippines and the disposition of the Philippine military bases are purely American affairs, but it is also willing to consider in good faith proposals to guarantee the neutrality and independence of the Philippines. (22nd Reuters Telegram)

The United States All Expresses Approval of US-Japan Understanding

Solemn Treaties Have Been Broken

Giving Opportunities to Resolve Disputes

(Washington) Today, the U.S. government and Congress continued to give good criticism to the exchange of letters between Secretary of State Hull and Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota. According to Democratic Representative Pope, "Japan has broken the solemn treaties it has concluded with us, but if Japan can resolve disputes with us through negotiation, I am willing to give it an opportunity to rehabilitate itself, because we really want peace." Representative Berkman also said, if Japan really wants to resolve disputes with us, then the United States may as well accommodate it. Representative Connolly spoke from the standpoint of cotton production and sales, saying that since Japan is the largest customer of American cotton, the United States does not need to provoke it. Japan and the United States mutually trade cotton and raw silk, which are mutually satisfactory, and hope that the two countries can reach a compromise. American people all express their approval of the exchange of letters between Hirota and Secretary of State Hull. The Washington Evening Star, a moderate American newspaper, published news of the negotiations between Japan and the United States in a prominent position, and there is also a long commentary, which said that Japan and the United States are ready to join hands, regardless of each other's past suspicions and fears. The Washington Daily said that the exchange of letters between the US and Japan is creating a new era of Pacific friendship. (22nd National Telegram)

Horiuchi Talks About American Feelings Toward Japan

Actual Problems Are Still in the Back

(Tokyo) Former Consul General in New York, Horiuchi Kensuke, was appointed Director of the Research Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and Director of the American Bureau. He returned to Japan from the United States this morning on the Chichibu Maru. According to the conversation, the US President and Secretary of State meet with reporters several times a week, but have never mentioned the Far East issue, so the American people have not received major stimuli. The United States is currently busy revitalizing the national industry and does not seem to value the Far East issue or the naval issue. When Foreign Minister Hirota took office, the American court and the opposition paid attention to what Hirota's diplomatic policy would be. However, the foreign minister's diplomatic speech outside the parliament, the appointment of Ambassador Saito to the United States, and the smooth progress of the fisheries negotiations on the Sino-Eastern Railway issue, etc., can make Americans understand that Japan has no intention of invading other countries (?). Therefore, although rumors of an emergency in the Far East spread from Moscow for a time, American feelings towards Japan have improved and they do not consider it a major problem. As for political issues such as the recognition of "Manchukuo", they have not yet appeared on the surface. (23rd Jiji Telegram)

Yokohama Horiuchi Kensuke, who was promoted from Consul General in New York to Director of the Research Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and Chief of the American Section, arrived in Yokohama at 7:30 this morning on the postal ship Chichibu Maru. The person spoke to reporters visiting him on the ship as follows. The relationship between Japan and the United States has recently taken a turn for the better, one reason being that Roosevelt is focusing on domestic issues, and the result of deeply understanding Foreign Minister Hirota's diplomacy. At present, President Roosevelt is taking a wait-and-see attitude towards the Far East issue, and there is less political criticism in the press on the issue of the "Manchukuo" implementing an imperial system. Also, there are more powerful opinions that discussions on naval issues are premature, and that various negotiations between Japan and the United States on practical issues are still in the back. (23rd Den-tsu Telegram)

Japan Tempts the United States

Promising Three Rights

Tokugawa Returns to Japan After a Visit to the United States

That is, Ambassador Saito was ordered to inquire about the true opinions of the United States. If the United States intends to recognize it, the Japanese side will make a secret agreement with the United States on the following three principles: (1) Japan is willing to reiterate that "Manchukuo" abides by the principles of open door and equal opportunity; (2) Japan is willing to recognize the superior position of the United States in its activities in North China; (3) Japan is willing to protect American investment in North China and "Manchukuo" in cooperation with the United States. (23rd China United Telegram)

San Francisco Prince Tokugawa Yumi's visit to the United States was a success and he returned to Japan by ship today. The results of this trip made him believe that Canada, Japan, and the United States can not only maintain their existing friendship, but will also strengthen the relationship of friendship and emotion. (22nd National Telegram)

Russian Newspaper Comments on the Meaning of Philippine Independence

Not Permitting True Independence

(Moscow) The United States House of Representatives has passed the Philippine Independence Act. *Pravda* comments on it, saying that the Philippine Islands occupy an extremely important military position. The main purpose of this proposal is nothing more than to ensure the neutrality of the Philippines through special international treaties. There is no doubt that this treaty will hinder Japan from seizing the Philippines. Furthermore, the United States does not allow the Philippines to have true independence. The proposal also reserves its right to maintain naval bases in the Philippines, while at the same time prohibiting Philippine sugar from being imported into the United States (this is what American sugar producers have resolutely demanded). This is the essence of the proposal, it is said. (TASS dispatch, 22nd)

British Attitude Towards Japan

Chamberlain Still Yearns for the Old Alliance

Says There Are No Irresolvable Disputes Between the Two Countries

(London) The British Chancellor of the Exchequer, Chamberlain, said in a speech in Newcastle today that various British businesses are now showing signs of recovery, more so than any other country. He also said that he did not believe that there were any irresolvable disputes between Britain and Japan, and that the two empires were bound together by mutual respect, many years of friendship, and the old alliance. (Reuters dispatch, 22nd)

(London) Regarding the two issues of Japanese goods dumping and the breakdown of Anglo-Japanese cotton industry negotiations, two ministers expressed their opinions today. The Minister of Commerce, Runciman, declared in the House of Commons regarding the impact of this issue on unemployment, saying that abandoning the Anglo-Japanese commercial treaty would be a great mistake. Runciman said, "Improving our commercial relations with Japan is indeed necessary, but we should not act rashly, lest the harm outweigh the benefits." Conversely, the Chancellor of the Exchequer, Chamberlain, said in a speech in Newcastle, "The situation of Japanese goods dumping is indeed worrying. If Britain does not take appropriate protective measures, the position of the Lancashire cotton industry will become increasingly serious. We really cannot make concessions beyond a certain limit. This is very obvious. However, I do not abandon hope, because I do not believe that there are any serious differences of opinion between the two great powers of Britain and Japan that cannot be avoided," and so on. (Havas dispatch, 23rd)

Japanese Diet Questions Brazil's Anti-Japanese Issue

Minister Nagai Replies:

It is the Government's Responsibility to Encourage Foreign Immigration and Trade

(Tokyo) The House of Representatives held a plenary session at 1:17 PM on the 23rd, during which Nakamura Yoshiki of the Government Friends Association raised a question:

Recently, the anti-Japanese sentiment in Brazil has become quite strong. There are currently about 170,000 Japanese in Brazil, and it is a suitable place for Japanese development in the future. How should the government try to promptly abolish the Brazilian anti-Japanese immigration bill? What is the government's future belief regarding this point? Please give a clear answer.

Minister Nagai replied:

Japanese immigrants are the most outstanding members of agricultural immigrants in the world and possess a spirit of peace. Especially for immigrants to South America, besides coexisting and prospering with the Brazilian people, they have no other intentions. Anyone close to Japanese immigrants can understand this. Even elementary school education is completely the same as that of Brazilian nationals. Other things can be imagined. Some people who do not understand the actual situation are now rising up to oppose Japan. We will cooperate with the foreign affairs authorities to explain the misunderstanding. Although it is very difficult to solve the population problem, I believe that both foreign immigration and foreign trade should be encouraged in an integrated manner, so as to make them understand that Japanese immigration is where we are striving, and so on. (Japan United Press dispatch, 23rd)

Britain Plans to Open New Air Route

Direct to the Far East Via Canada

Air Service to Start This Summer

(London) The *Daily Telegraph* reports that Britain is currently consulting with Canada and New York-Finland to establish a new airmail route between Britain and the Far East. The air service will begin this summer, with a speed unmatched to date. According to this plan, the mail-carrying aircraft will be loaded onto ships at a point west of Ireland, cross the Atlantic Ocean, and then leave the ship again at "Meisdao" at the mouth of the St. Lawrence River in eastern Canada, and fly across the American continent to the Far East. (Havas dispatch, 23rd)

One of the First Supplementary Plans

(Tokyo) The submarine tender "Taigei," which the Yokosuka Naval Arsenal began building in 1932, has now been completed. It was originally scheduled to be completed next year, but in view of the increasingly urgent world situation for Japan, work was accelerated and completed ahead of schedule. The Navy of Siam

Only Eight Warships Applicable

Khamtai. The Siamese naval magazine recently published an article entitled "Our Navy," which describes the past and present of the Siamese Navy in detail, saying that the purpose of the Siamese Navy is not like that of the great powers who want to seize maritime hegemony, but only to defend themselves. Because the coastline of Siam is 1,500 miles long, if something happens one day, and the ports are blocked, panic will be seen in less than seven days. Therefore, Siam needs a proper navy for self-defense, which is obvious and urgent. However, although Siam has continued to try to improve after the naval defeat in 1873, its strength is still thin, and the construction of the ships has been a long time. Generally, each ship is only sufficient for 20 years, submarines for 15 years, and destroyers for only 5 to 10 years. An investigation in January of this year revealed that only eight warships are applicable. (Hualian dispatch, 23rd)

Negotiations on the Tangshan Labor Strike Have Not Yet Yielded Results

Workers Patrol the Streets and Stores Close Their Doors

Public Security Bureau Still Maintaining Strict Guard

Mining Assistant Manager Goes to Mediate

Workers Form United Autonomous General Labor Union

(Tianjin) Gu Zhen, the assistant manager of the Kailuan Mining Bureau, went to Tangshan on the 23rd with Xu Huidong, director of the People's Movement Section of the Hebei Party Department, to deal with the labor strike. The Belgian ambassador to Ping visited Huang Fu on the 23rd and inquired about the measures to deal with the Tangshan labor strike. Zhao Xun, director of the Tangshan Public Security Bureau, invited Zhao Dazhong, a workers' representative, again on the 23rd to discuss the settlement of the labor strike, but there were no results. On the 23rd, the miners in the Tangshan mine still worked underground under the leadership of the Belgian engineer. The mine police protected the wells to prevent accidents. On the 23rd, the workers of the Majiagou and Zhaogezhuang mines stated that they had not sent representatives to participate in the strike activities of the Tangshan mine workers. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

(Tianjin) On the 23rd, the striking workers in Tangshan organized a workers' united team, divided into three brigades, each with three companies. The workers wore red cloth strips with the brigade number written on them, and carried wooden sticks and iron rods, patrolling the streets with the inspectors. Seeing the tense situation, the merchants closed their doors completely again. The workers submitted twelve articles to the Public Security Bureau, requesting a response. The Public Security Bureau remained closed and guarded. On the afternoon of the 23rd, the striking workers demanded that the contractors provide food and drinks, requiring them to be prepared within five hours. The contractors did not comply, and the workers gathered to surround the contractors' residences, intending to use force. The mine police rushed to the scene and dispersed them. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

(Tianjin) On the 23rd, the striking workers in Tangshan gathered at the Tianhe Inn west of the station to hold a meeting and formed the Hebei Province War Zone Miners' United Autonomous General Labor Union and the Labor-Capital Cooperation General Association. Zhao Dazhong was elected as the chairman and Zhao Banchao as the secretary. After the meeting, it was decided to set up an office. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

(Tianjin) On the 23rd, the Kailuan Mining Bureau sent a letter to various newspapers, stating the truth of the Tangshan mining strike. The letter stated that the mining company signed a draft agreement with the previous strike representatives, which did not include promises to pay 40 days of Zhenjing expenses and blood and sweat labor funds, nor did it promise to increase wages for the workers. This time, a small number of workers were instigated to strike, and the government has taken measures to stop it. The reason for the workers' strike was a conflict with the representatives and had nothing to do with the mining company. However, the mining company is suffering losses for a long time, which is really not good. It is determined to make every effort to quell the strike. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

The Western Xinjiang Railway Project

Expected to be Completed in the 26th Year of the Republic

(Nanjing) Commissioner Chuan Rulin proposed the construction of the Xi'an-Xinjiang Railway. The Executive Yuan handed over the planning to the Ministry of Railways, Transportation, Finance, and Industry. The road is divided into twenty sections, from Xi'an to Lanzhou, divided into two sections, and from Lanzhou to Tacheng divided into eighteen sections. The road starts in Xi'an and ends in Tacheng. The Longhai Railway is limited to be fully completed in the 24th year of the Republic. Therefore, the project will start construction in the 25th year of the Republic. The Western Xinjiang Road and the Longhai Road are connected, and it is expected to be completed in the 26th year of the Republic. The project plans to adopt a military-industrial policy. Overview of National Consolidated Taxes

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance reports that the currently collected national consolidated tax area includes a total of nine provinces. Among them, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui form one district, Jiangxi, Hunan, and Hubei form one district, and Shandong and Henan form one district. Each district has a director-general. A branch office is set up in Fuzhou. The consolidated taxes of the remaining provinces are still collected and used by the local administrative organs and have not been submitted to the central government. The total revenue of various national consolidated taxes in the 22nd year of the Republic (1933) is estimated to be: (1) Cigarette tax of 58 million yuan, (2) Cotton yarn tax of 20 million yuan, (3) Wheat flour tax of 5 million yuan, (4) Match tax of 4 million yuan, (5) Cement tax of 860,000 yuan, totaling 87.86 million yuan. Since December 15th of last year, after increasing the tax rates on matches, cigarettes, and cement (averaging an increase of one-third), it is expected that an additional 20 million yuan can be collected this year. (23rd dispatch)

The meeting adjourned at noon, followed by a banquet hosted by the Jingye Film Association. In the afternoon, they paid respects at the mausoleum and resumed the meeting at 3 p.m. Shao Yuanchong delivered a speech, stating that in the future, the film industry should strive for both quantitative increase and, more importantly, qualitative improvement. Strict attention should be paid to ideological issues, and more films should be produced to awaken national spirit and strive for the government's production and construction work. Scientific knowledge should be promoted to the people, and China's inherent morality should be advocated. Imitating foreign films that only focus on sensual content should be avoided, and so on. Chen Guofu also telegraphed, stating that in the future, the film industry should prioritize the nation and the people, understand the relationship between film and social education, and devote efforts to the compilation of educational films. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 23rd)

Page 9

Current Commentary

Observations on the US-Japan Understanding (Ang Ruo)

The resolution of international issues involves no more than three paths: diplomatic negotiations, armed intervention, and war. The Washington Conference succeeded and the Shandong issue was resolved. This is one example of an international issue resolved through diplomatic negotiations. The intervention of Russia, France, and Germany in the return of Liaoning is also a clear demonstration of armed mediation. As for war, it is the last resort after diplomatic failure and the failure of intervention. Given the warnings of the dangers of war and the fear of unpredictable outcomes, unless one harbors a狂妄 psychological desire for military aggression or is forced into a dangerous situation where the foundation of the nation is shaken, one is unwilling to easily make a desperate gamble. Since the Balkan issue led to an unprecedented world war, the world has been exhausting itself in the arduous task of reconstruction. Since war is not possible and peace cannot be achieved, the Far Eastern issue has fallen into a stalemate.

Recently, the exchange of documents between Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota and U.S. Secretary of State Hull has been published, shocking the world. This is indeed a major turning point in US-Japan relations and a major key to the future of the Far Eastern issue. It has the same profound meaning as the re-establishment of diplomatic relations between the US and Russia. To what extent the US-Japan understanding has reached and to what situation it will evolve in the future, outsiders have no way of judging. However, our diplomatic authorities should be vigilant and prepare for how to deal with it, which seems self-evident.

Various parties have already made various speculations about this US-Japan understanding. In fact, in our observation, this is just the beginning of a negotiation to bring the extremely thorny Far Eastern issue, which is gradually falling into the crisis of a second world war, into diplomatic negotiations. The issue itself still needs to be negotiated in the future. Changes are unpredictable. As for whether it can be resolved and how it will be resolved, it is still difficult to say. Even President Roosevelt and Foreign Minister Hirota may not have this confidence.

The issues raised in the telegram regarding the initial US-Japan understanding include the US revising its immigration laws, abandoning naval bases in the Philippines, and recognizing the puppet state. Japan will exchange this for maintaining the current 5:5:3 naval ratio. The path of negotiation requires waiting for Japanese Ambassador to the US Saito to return to Tokyo for consultations, and then holding a naval conference next year. At the same time, a second Pacific Conference will be held. The countries participating in the conference, in addition to the US, UK, China, Japan, France, Italy, Netherlands, Belgium, and Portugal, which signed the Nine-Power Treaty, will also include Soviet Russia, which has a close relationship with the Far Eastern issue. It is still remembered that when the League of Nations failed to handle the Northeast issue, some people advocated convening a conference of the Nine-Power Treaty countries. The Far Eastern situation has been deadlocked until now. Either a general resolution will be made through war, or the only other way is a second Washington Conference to make a compromise diplomatic resolution.

For now, we will leave aside the immigration issue, the Philippine issue, and the naval ratio issue, which are only of secondary importance to us. Let's try to speculate on the so-called issue of recognizing the puppet state. The US's Far Eastern policy is based on two major foundations: the Open Door Policy and the Nine-Power Treaty. The starting point of these two major basic policies is directed at Japan. The Paris Peace Conference failed to make Japan return Shandong to us. American public opinion was greatly shocked. Wilson's policy failed because of this. Our country refused to sign the Treaty of Versailles. The US Senate also did not approve it. The degree of deterioration in US-Japan relations at that time was similar to today. When the Pacific Conference established the Nine-Power Treaty, the first article stipulated that "Respect the sovereignty, independence, and territorial and administrative integrity of China." It also said, "Shall not take advantage of the situation in China to seek special rights, reduce the rights of the people of friendly countries, and shall not encourage actions harmful to the safety of friendly countries." Article 2 of the treaty stipulates that "The contracting countries agree not to conclude treaties or agreements, or understandings, alone or jointly with any one or more countries, that would infringe or hinder the principles mentioned in Article 1." The puppet state was created by Japan alone to cover up its aggression. This has become a settled case in the international community. In our country's internal affairs, Puyi's usurpation constitutes an act of rebellion. Although international relations are extremely unpredictable, and President Roosevelt has repeatedly announced to us with extraordinary actions, it is beyond our logical imagination to say that he will overturn all Stimson Doctrine, League of Nations resolutions, and even the Nine-Power Treaty, without obtaining the consent of friendly countries and regardless of the serious consequences, and directly recognize the puppet state as a means of promoting his own recovery.

A Washington dispatch says, "Observers believe that all countries related to the Far East should participate in the US-Japan discussions. It also said that the US expressed in its reply that the resolution of the Pacific issue must be bound by existing treaties, because this is a multilateral issue and not simply a bilateral issue between the US and Japan. There are many speculations here about the act of recognizing 'Manchukuo'. It is believed that the US may not take this action without the participation of China and Soviet Russia." This is indeed a talk close to the truth. From this, it can be seen that the US still has no intention of tearing up existing treaties. Japan's actions, however, violate existing treaties everywhere. Therefore, to try to resolve the Far Eastern issue with the spirit and text of international treaties without contradicting them, how far away is the time to seek a resolution with related countries?

According to a London telegram, the UK welcomes the US-Japan understanding. It also claims that the US will first advise our country to be the one who unties the bell, and the promotion of the ambassadors of various countries stationed in China to ambassadors will be used as an exchange. Then the crux of the problem still lies in our country's taking good care of itself.

Solving Economic Difficulties Lies in Focusing on Far East Trade

Borah's Extraneous Remarks Involve the Silver Issue

Grain Monopoly Considered an Urgent Task

(Washington) Today, Senator Borah delivered a speech at the Foreign Policy Conference, criticizing the government's reduction of grain production, saying that millions of Americans are currently suffering from hunger. If Americans want to remedy today's unstable phenomenon, they must urgently manage grain production. Under the goal of revitalizing the United States, grain monopoly is an urgent task. If the United States wants to solve its financial problems, it must be good at coping with foreign trade. The United States' assumed markets in the future are in the East and Soviet Russia. There is a major clause that must be considered in the current trend, that is, the method of making money by using foreign trade is the common practice of these countries in the past two years. Borah's speech has attracted the attention of the financial community, because the unspoken meaning involves the silver issue. (National Telegram on the 23rd)

(Washington) Today, the silver bill began to proceed in the House again. It was found that four days after the House passed Darcey's bill, the supporters of the silver bill transferred the proposals of Goldwater and Bullock and the amendments of Schickele from the subcommittee to the House Banking and Currency Committee, and obtained a favorable report. It is said that some people have asked the Banking and Currency Committee to immediately study the bill and amendments so that they can be submitted to the parliament as soon as possible. Goldwater's proposal is the more important bill in this session of Congress's silver bill. This bill proposes the establishment of a monetary committee, whose members are the Minister of Finance, the President of the Federal Reserve, and three people appointed by the President. If the price of goods is higher or lower than the standard price in one year, the monetary committee may increase or decrease the gold content of the US dollar to limit it. Schickele's amendment is to suggest to the Ministry of Finance to purchase at least 50,000,000 ounces of silver per month until the purchase of silver reaches 1,000,000,000 ounces, or the gold-silver ratio reaches a ratio of sixteen to one. The silver certificates issued by the government will be determined by the amount of silver purchased by the government. (National Telegram on the 23rd)

Southern Ireland Abolishes the Senate

Dublin After the Senate rejected the bill banning blue shirt uniforms, today, Executive Chairman de Valera proposed a bill to abolish the Senate in Parliament. Although the opposition party opposed this bill, it was finally passed by a vote of 59 to 43. de Valera declared that the Senate, under its current organization, is a burden on the country, and the Senate's rejection of the blue shirt bill further shows that the Senate is deliberately preventing the government from fulfilling its duties. (Reuters telegram on the 22nd)

British Cabinet Studies Continuing Disarmament Negotiations

Choose One of Three Methods

(London) This morning, the cabinet members held a meeting, based on the report submitted by Eden's tour of Europe and the recent communication from France, to study the disarmament issue. In order to continue the disarmament negotiations, the cabinet should choose one of the following three methods: (1) The meeting of the minority committee of the Disarmament Conference's Presidium will still be held on April 10th, and the British representative will be instructed to propose convening the General Committee. Germany has already recognized the British disarmament plan as the basis for discussion, so if the General Committee meets, the German representative is expected to participate. (2) Secondly, only convene a smaller meeting of countries that are particularly concerned, so that the disarmament issue can be more easily resolved. (3) Thirdly, only bilateral negotiations will continue to be conducted between the two countries. Which of the above three will be chosen must be determined after the Cabinet Disarmament Committee meeting on Monday makes an explanation. However, the general opinion at present is most in favor of the first method (Havas on the 22nd)

Germany Trains Party Army

Formulates Three Types of Badges

(Berlin) Non-governmental Cabinet Minister and Chief of Staff of the National Socialist Party Army Roehm has recently formulated three types of physical education badges for the Party Army, which are awarded in grades according to the level of training of the Party Army. These badges are practically equivalent to the army's military ranks. The first type is made of copper and can be awarded to any German people "who meet the qualifications for joining the army." The so-called qualifications are that they have been examined by a doctor, interviewed by the Party Army captain, and tested in the field. The second type is made of silver and is awarded to anyone who passes the instructor's examination. The third type is made of gold and is dedicated to the captains of each stormtrooper team. The physical training of the Party Army includes racing, throwing, hand grenades, shooting targets with small-caliber firearms, and walking in the field with military uniforms. Those who have been awarded badges by the Party Army have the obligation to be summoned whenever the leader calls. (Havas on the 22nd)

Roosevelt's Mediation is Gradually Working

Major Disturbance Occurs in New York

Today's meeting was very interesting and gratifying. When the meeting was in progress, President Roosevelt often laughed, which could be heard outside the room, showing the optimism of the meeting. At the same time, the 12,000 dockworkers were said to be on strike, but because President Roosevelt advised them to postpone their action, the dockworkers' strike will not occur for the time being. (Reuters telegram on the 22nd)

The union leaders also held a meeting at the AFL building at night, resolving to extend the strike time by 48 hours so that the President would have time to consider how to decide on the workers' demands. According to reports, the demands of automobile workers are to have the right to form their own unions without being affiliated with the owners' associations. (Havas telegram on the 22nd)

Union leaders replied that they did not want to incite a strike, but demanded immediate concrete measures to resolve this dispute. (Reuters telegram on the 22nd)

In the riots in lower New York City, mounted police tried to disperse the crowd, but were attacked by 3,000 strikers. Then the riots followed. All taxi drivers who did not support the strike were detained, and drivers and passengers were brutally beaten. Twenty-five passengers were knocked to the ground and lost consciousness. Thirty cars were destroyed into pieces, and ten policemen were also injured. (Havas telegram on the 22nd)

This morning, in order to prevent further bloodshed, a large team of New York police gathered on Times Street, Broadway Road, and 42nd Street. The Mayor of New York also issued a notice, advising the strikers not to cause further disturbances, and said that the strikers were being incited by rioters. (Reuters telegram on the 22nd)

The Tragic State of the Hakodate Fire

More Than 90,000 People Homeless

Authorities Begin Handling the Aftermath

Actual Number of Dead and Injured (Tokyo) Regarding the Hakodate fire, the Ministry of Home Affairs made the following public announcement at 9:00 PM on the 22nd:

The fire started at 6:30 PM on the 21st and was extinguished at 7:00 AM the following morning. The cause of the fire is unknown. 23,600 houses were burned down. 652 people died. 450 people were injured. Hundreds of people who fled to the seashore were swept away by storm waves. 92,000 people are homeless.

Upon receiving the report of the great fire, the police department immediately dispatched 180 police officers. The 7th Division also sent troops to help maintain order, and public safety was gradually restored. The origin of the fire was the Fukuda-ya Fireworks Manufacturer in Yachigashira-cho. Important buildings that were burned down include the Hakodate Police Station, the Hakodate City Hall, the 12th Bank, the Chamber of Commerce, the Civic Hall, the Hakodate District Court, and the Hakodate Tax Office. There are three causes for the great fire: (1) At the time of the fire, there was a gale with a speed of about 18 meters per second due to the influence of a low-pressure system moving from the Sea of Japan to the central part of Hokkaido; (2) Most of the Hakodate topography is sloping; (3) The roads were too narrow. (23rd Dispatch from Dentsu)

Cause of the Fire Although there is a theory that the cause of the great fire was a chimney being blown down, according to one report, the municipal authorities and citizens were in a dispute over the reduction of electricity fees, which had escalated to the point of a breakdown in talks. Many residents participated in an electricity boycott alliance and used kerosene lamps, leading to carelessness. (23rd Dispatch from Rengo)

Scene Photographs Hakodate After the great fire, a special correspondent from Dentsu, who entered the scene at great risk, telegraphed the tragic situation in the city, saying, "The city is completely leveled. In the ruins, mothers are looking for their children and wives are looking for their husbands, their faces washed with tears. Their misery cannot be described in words. Only iron-framed buildings and fireproof warehouses still stand proudly. At night, the whole city is dark, and only the swords of the garrison soldiers shine. The bodies of those who were burned to death are being collected in parks and elementary schools. Crows and magpies are already flocking to the corpses along the coast, fighting to eat them. The disaster victims are destitute, some wearing only underclothes. Added to that, it is snowing, and there is concern about freezing and starvation." (23rd Dispatch from Dentsu)

No Way to Escape (Tokyo) According to a special correspondent from the Rengo News Agency who telegraphed from Hakodate, the Hakodate fire was just like the great Tokyo earthquake of previous years. Because of the fierceness of the fire, whirlwinds occurred everywhere, and pillars of fire soared into the sky. Groups of refugees ran under the pillars of fire, resembling a living hell. Residents in the western part of the city were able to evacuate more easily due to the advantageous terrain, and there were fewer deaths and injuries. However, the residents in the eastern part of the city first evacuated to the open space on the coast, but then a sudden change in wind direction occurred. The refugees had the raging sea behind them and the raging fire coming at them from the front. There was nowhere to escape, resulting in total destruction. More than 100,000 citizens were homeless, standing alone on the streets. By daybreak, the wind and snow were mixed, and people were continually suffering from frostbite, a very tragic scene. (23rd Dispatch from Rengo)

Relief Efforts Hakodate Hakodate Mayor Sakamoto convened an emergency city council on the charred earth on the afternoon of the 22nd to discuss ways to help the disaster victims. Relief efforts began immediately. The Railway Bureau made arrangements to give preferential treatment to disaster victims traveling by train. Because many of the shipping company's crew members lived in Hakodate and their whereabouts were unknown, they were working hard to recruit crew members. Although there were as many as 100,000 disaster victims, the order in the city was not disturbed, making it relatively easy for the authorities to maintain public safety. (23rd Dispatch from Rengo)

Hakodate The anxiety of the victims has gradually decreased since contact was established with the mainland and relief supplies were transported in. White smoke still lingers in the embers. Everywhere, people are searching for bodies and treating the injured. In the meantime, lumber and other materials have been transported from various places. Thatched huts are being built in the city as temporary shelter. Reconstruction has also begun. (23rd Dispatch from Dentsu)

(Tokyo) The Japanese government has decided to exempt refugees in Hakodate from taxes for one year, that is, to completely exempt income tax and business income tax in the disaster area. The bill will be submitted to both houses within days. The government also recognizes that the great fire has provided a great lesson in national defense and has decided to thoroughly study future fire prevention measures. (23rd Dispatch from Hualian)

Fire Insurance Claims (Tokyo) The Fire Insurance Association will hold a meeting at 2:00 PM today to discuss the payment of Hakodate fire insurance claims. Insurance Department Director Ishii from the Ministry of Commerce and Industry will attend the meeting. As a result of the negotiations, it was decided to begin paying out claims immediately. The total amount of claims paid out due to the Hakodate fire by Japanese and foreign insurance companies is approximately 15 million Japanese yen. (23rd Dispatch from Dentsu)

Maritime Administration Discussion Conference

Load Line Convention Proposal Submitted for Review

(Nanjing) The Maritime Administration Discussion Conference convened by the Ministry of Communications held its first meeting on the morning of the 23rd. Gao Tingzi chaired the meeting, which discussed (2) the proposal to reform the maritime administration agencies, totaling seven proposals. It was resolved to leave them with the ministry for reference. (2) The load line convention proposal, including Proposal A to promptly implement the ship load line regulations and Proposal B, the detailed rules for the implementation of the load line regulations, were discussed together. Peng Hu, director of the Shanghai Maritime Administration Bureau, suggested forming a special committee to study implementation. Gao Tingzi proposed (1) inviting experts to translate the International Load Line Convention, and (2) drafting detailed rules for the implementation of the load line regulations, taking into account China's special circumstances. It was resolved to submit them to experts such as Liu Fupei for review. The second meeting was held in the afternoon, and resolutions were passed to strictly enforce the Ship Act, promulgate regulations on the protection of maritime administration personnel and incentive measures, expand maritime administration work, and implement the legal inspection of foreign ships. It was decided to continue the third meeting on the 24th to discuss the recovery of inland river maritime administration, the adjustment of finance, and the establishment of additional naval courts. The conference is scheduled to close next month. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Communications Maritime Administration Discussion Conference was held at the ministry on the morning of the 23rd. Division Chief Gao Tingzi chaired the meeting, first reporting the significance of the meeting and the work situation of each bureau. The meeting continued in the afternoon, discussing a total of 26 proposals. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM. The meeting will continue for one day on the 25th. There are a total of 39 proposals, the content of which is divided into seven categories: organization of maritime administration agencies, compilation of maritime administration laws and regulations, talent training and protection, waterway consolidation, load line law, and expansion of maritime administration work. Hebei and Shandong Provinces Increase Match Tax

The Ministry Sets Two Compromise Measures

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance, considering that match manufacturers in Hebei and Shandong provinces are unable to bear the increased match tax, and in order to take into account commercial conditions, has proposed two compromise measures and issued a general order to match manufacturers in Hebei and Shandong provinces to temporarily implement them on a trial basis: (1) For each small box of Grade A sulfurized phosphorus matches produced by factories in Shandong Province, the original 80 sticks are changed to 85 sticks, and for Grade B matches, they are changed to 115 sticks. The tax is still paid according to the established tax rate. (2) Before the modification of each small box containing more than 90 matches in Hebei Province, a one-sixth refund of the tax revenue may be obtained, that is, the Grade A tax rate of 10 yuan and 8 jiao per case will be reduced by 1 yuan and 8 jiao. (23rd Dispatch from Central News Agency)

Yang Xiaocang Talks About His Impressions of Traveling in Japan

(Nanjing) Yang Xiaocang, the military attaché of the Chinese Embassy in Japan, resigned from his position due to illness and came to Nanjing. According to him: (1) Since the Sino-Japanese diplomatic relations had disputes, the overseas Chinese in Japan felt all kinds of oppression and it was difficult to describe. The recent situation has been eased compared to before. (2) It is rumored that both China and Japan will temporarily shelve the Northeast issue and discuss the outstanding Sino-Japanese cases first. Because I left Japan almost a month ago, the recent situation is not very clear. I am serving as a military attache and have rarely asked about diplomacy. But according to my personal observations, it is still too early to talk about resolving outstanding cases. (3) After the so-called "Manchurian Government" was organized in the three eastern provinces and declared itself emperor on March 1, the Japanese were ecstatic, and it was painful to say. (4) I have been subjected to all kinds of stimuli in Japan. Last year, I suffered from gastrointestinal disease for half a year. I have repeatedly requested to resign, and now it has been approved. I have telegraphed Chairman Jiang in Ganzhou, and will go to Ganzhou to report to him and report the past history of serving as a military attache in the museum after receiving his reply. It has not been decided whether or not to visit Wang, who also serves as the Minister of Foreign Affairs, because I am in charge of military affairs. I plan to return to Beiping for recuperation in the near future. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Industry previously distributed rural economic survey forms, ordering the responsible agencies in various provinces and cities to fill them out and report them. The provinces and cities that have reported include Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Hebei, Fujian, Anhui, Guangxi, and Qinghai, totaling several hundred counties. (23rd Dispatch from Central News Agency)

Dai Chuanxian's Mission to the Northwest

(Nanjing) Dai Chuanxian and Song Ziwen are scheduled to depart for the Northwest on the 28th, first to Luoyang and then to Shaanxi. According to Xu Chonghao, the Secretary-General of the Examination Yuan, Dai's mission this time is: (1) to inspect transportation and water conservancy, with the Wei Canal and the roads in northern and southern Shaanxi as the main focus; (2) to investigate charitable relief work and plan future methods for disaster relief, local development, and rural animal husbandry; (3) to hold a groundbreaking ceremony for the Northwest Agricultural and Forestry College. Because the capital's general examination is scheduled to be held in Beijing on April 20, Dai must rush back to preside over it between the 20th and 25th of next month. (23rd Dispatch from Central News Agency)

The Ministry of Industry Restricts the Issuance of Fishing Vessel Fishing Licenses

(Nanjing) Chen Tongbai and other representatives of the aquatic industry telegraphed the Ministry of Industry, saying that unscrupulous merchants were colluding with foreigners to organize large-scale fishing companies in Shanghai, hiring foreigners as captains and crew members. They requested that the issuance of fishing vessel fishing licenses be stopped. The ministry specially drafted measures to crack down on these activities and issued a general order to coastal agencies: (A) The applicant for a fishing license is limited to those with Republic of China nationality. If it is a company, the origin of its shareholders and capital should be investigated. (B) The fishing vessel should be examined for its purchase contract, or the construction contract, and its history. (C) The crew is limited to personnel of the Republic of China. (D) The captain should be checked for a Ministry of Industry registration certificate. If he has not been registered, he must attach qualification certificates. (E) The fishing vessel's anchorage port should be checked to see if it is within the jurisdiction. (23rd Special Dispatch)

The Ministry of Interior Orders All Provinces to Complete Local Autonomy Within a Time Limit

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Interior has ordered all provinces to complete local autonomy within a time limit, no later than the end of this year. (23rd Special Dispatch)

General Provisional Rules for Strictly Prohibiting the Sale and Slaughter of Working Cattle. Work is planned to begin in the spring and be completed before the flood season. It is estimated that the cost of revetment protection, transportation equipment, and subsidies for military labor will total more than 837,000 yuan. It has been submitted to the Central Government for allocation. After the funds arrive, please assign troops to carry out the work. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Jinan) Li Shuchun and He Siyuan visited the Rural Construction Research Institute in Zouping on the morning of the 22nd and returned to Jinan in the afternoon. They said that the politics of the counties they had passed through had greatly improved. Compared with the 70% and 30% ratio of 1931, the county magistrates were all competent. The police administration of Guangrao, Changshan, and Huantai was the best. In other counties, the older county magistrates, Qidong and Bo, were the best with the militia. Changshan, Shouguang, Guangrao, Qingcheng, Zichuan, and Boshan were second best. Huantai and Changle were next best. The public security bureau of Qidong was the best. Education in Huantai was the most popular. Zichuan had the most complete elementary schools. Changshan's county middle school was the best in terms of science. Overall, Gaoyuan's education was the most advanced. Each county's prison is preparing to build a new prison civilian factory, but the goods are not easy to sell. The customs of each county are simple and honest. Boshan needs a large power plant. (22nd Special Dispatch)

丨Special Commercial Report from Reuters, March 23rd丨

Gold and Silver: London Gold Price: Today (23rd), the London gold price is 136 shillings, down 2 pence from yesterday.

London Silver Bars: This morning (23rd), the London silver market was stable. Spot prices were 20 pence, and futures were 20 pence and 0.0625, both up 0.0125, mainly due to slight purchases from China.

New York Silver Bars: Today (23rd), the silver market was calm and not very noticeable, but it was firm due to rising prices in London and Shanghai. There were no white silver reports from Washington, which is the reason for the light silver market. Prices are stable at 35 pounds sterling below London. Futures rose from zero to twenty pounds sterling from yesterday's close.

Bombay Silver Bars: Today (23rd), the Bombay silver market closed stable. Spot prices rose 6 annas to 55 rupees and 4 annas.

Exchange Rates: British-American Exchange Rate: This morning (23rd), the London foreign exchange market was very light. The opening exchange rate between British and American currencies was $5.1125, the same as yesterday's closing exchange rate between the US and the UK. The price fluctuation was very small before noon. The latest price is $5.109375. Also, one US dollar is equivalent to 3 shillings and 10.972 pence in British gold.

British-French Exchange Rate: The opening price was 77 francs 40, the same as yesterday's price. There have been no changes since.

US-UK Exchange Rate: The previous day's closing price for the New York exchange rate against the British pound was 5.11125. Today's opening price was 5.1075, second trading session 5.1175, third trading session 5.100, fourth trading session 5.100, fifth trading session 5.11625, sixth trading session 5.1375.

Cotton and Wheat: New York Cotton: Today (23rd), the New York cotton market was calm. Purchases by bankers, brokers, peers, and Japanese merchants absorbed scattered selling. Shortly after the opening, the market situation reacted slightly due to foreign selling. It is widely believed that India is selling.

Bombay Cotton: Today (23rd), the Bombay cotton market rose due to purchases by European exporters and relatively stable Liverpool prices. April-May Broach cotton was 197.5 rupees, up 2 rupees.

Liverpool Cotton: Today (23rd), the Liverpool cotton market was relatively firm. At 1:00 PM, the May futures price was 6.13, up 3 points from yesterday.

Liverpool Wheat: Today (23rd), Liverpool wheat for May delivery rose .25 to 4 shillings and 3.125 pence.

Rubber: London Rubber: Today, March 23rd, the London rubber market was light. At noon, the trading price for July-September delivery was 5.25 pence, down 32nd parts of a penny.

New York Rubber: Today (23rd), the New York rubber market was calm but stable due to foreign telegrams. Market participants are now awaiting news of restrictions and the development of the labor situation.

Securities: New York: Today (23rd), the securities market situation was mixed and sluggish, with a tendency towards easing. Although the automobile industry dispute showed signs of mediation, and the management case of the Securities Exchange also encountered significant opposition, there was still anxiety in the market, and prices rose and fell only slightly. Chinese and Japanese Representatives Negotiate the Luan River Area Problem in Tianjin

Tao Shangming, Chayama, Yiga, and Others Meet

Discussed for a Long Time at the Beining Railway Dormitory

Tianjin Correspondence: At 11:00 AM on the 20th, Chinese and Japanese representatives held an important meeting at the Beining Railway Bureau dormitory on Haihe Road in the Tianjin Special District. The Chinese side was represented by Tao Shangming, Administrative Inspector of the Luan-Yu District; Zhu Shiqin, Counselor of the Beiping Military Branch; and Yin Tong, Director of the Beining Railway Bureau. The Japanese side was represented by Chayama, Military Attaché of the Japanese Embassy in Ping; Yiga, Chief of the Yuguan Special Service Organ; and Ohashi, Staff Officer of the Japanese Army stationed in Tianjin. Chayama came to Tianjin from Ping on the 19th night, and Yiga rushed from Yuguan on the morning of the 20th. The focus of this meeting was that Japanese troops are stationed everywhere in the Luan River area, and Japanese and Korean residents are relocating to the interior of the pass in large numbers. The Chinese side feels that it cannot freely exercise local public security administration. If the Chinese and Japanese sides act independently, it is inevitable that misunderstandings will arise over time. Also, from the Shi River to Yuguan, the Japanese side has designated it as a garrison area for the Japanese army stationed in Shanhaiguan, and armed police and wartime security teams are not allowed to pass through. However, local ruffians in Shimentai, Taitouying, Jianchangying, and Saheqiao collude with external forces and commit many evils. The county magistrate lacks the strength to control them, so wartime security teams must be sent to patrol to deter them. Furthermore, Japanese troops are stationed at various stations along the Beining Railway from Tanggu to Shanhaiguan. Whenever vehicles enter the station, Japanese troops are deployed on the platform to perform their inspection and surveillance duties, which clearly conflicts with the authority of the Chinese police. Due to the unclear demarcation of boundaries at Shanhaiguan Station, there is often confusion in parking vehicles and managing trains. In addition, the crackdown on Japanese and Korean vagrants in the Luan River area and the rectification of public security were also the focus of this meeting. Previously, when Tao Shangming went to Ping, he had reached an agreement with Chayama to take advantage of Yiga's visit to Tianjin to meet with Umezu Mijiro to discuss matters with each other. Yin Tong also believed that a meeting was necessary. Therefore, on the morning of the 20th, they held talks for a long time at the Beining dormitory, and generally reached some results. Tao Shangming was unwilling to disclose the content of the meeting because the results had not yet been implemented, so it is difficult to know the actual extent of the discussions. (20th)

Yan Huijing Visits Chiang to Report on the International Situation

Chiang Finishes Meeting with Provincial Education Directors, Etc.
