丨 The Head of the Wuxi Public Security Bureau Refuses to Hand Over, Alleging Li as the Mastermind 丨

Liu Zhuomin, the Chief of the Second Branch of the Wuxi Road District Public Security Bureau, was recently dismissed from his post. Relying on Li Shuyun, the concubine of Gu Renfa, the Civil Affairs Director of Jiangsu Province, as his shield, he refused to hand over his duties. Upon receiving the news, the Civil Affairs Department ordered the arrest of Li Shuyun to investigate the case. Li Shuyun and her daughter were apprehended in Shanghai a few days ago and escorted to Wuxi yesterday. The following is a detailed account of the events.

Circumstances of Dismissal: Liu Zhuomin, the Chief of the Second Branch of the Wuxi Road District Public Security Bureau, had been in office for five months. His management of the bureau was lackluster and ineffective, resulting in no achievements. Consequently, Li Wengong, the Director of the County Public Security Bureau, suspended Liu from his duties and appointed Gao Chongshan, the current Chief of the First Branch, to fill the vacancy. However, Liu was appointed by the Civil Affairs Department, and his wife, Li Rongzhen, had sworn sisterhood with Li Shuyun, the concubine of Civil Affairs Director Gu Renfa, forging a close relationship. Therefore, after receiving the suspension order from the County Public Security Bureau, Chief Liu immediately instructed his wife, Li Rongzhen, to report the news to Gu's concubine, Li Shuyun, in Zhenjiang, urgently requesting assistance.

Earnest Entreaties: Gu's concubine, Li Shuyun, learned that Director Gu had been summoned to the Nanchang Headquarters by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek for training and had not yet returned to Zhenjiang. In her haste, she could not think of a solution, so she accompanied Secretary Xiao and left Zhenjiang immediately, arriving in Wuxi on the 14th and staying at the New World Hotel. When Liu Zhuomin heard the news, he and his wife went to greet them eagerly, treating them to a Western meal at a Western restaurant, accompanied by Peng Xiweng, the Chief of the Fifth Branch. During the meal, Liu earnestly pleaded with Li Shuyun to find a solution for him. Li agreed without hesitation and told Liu to relax and wait for Director Gu to return to the province and revoke the order.

Refusal to Hand Over: The next day, Li Shuyun left Wuxi for Shanghai. On the morning of the 15th, Director Li of the Public Security Bureau, knowing that the order had been issued for several days, ordered Inspector Zhang Yu to accompany the newly appointed Chief Gao Chongshan to take over the office. However, Liu Zhuomin, feeling confident, refused to hand over the office, saying, "Director Gu sent me here. If I am to be dismissed, I must wait for the Director's order to arrive before I hand over the office."

Armed Takeover: Inspector Zhang and others had no choice but to report the situation back to Director Li. Upon hearing this, Li was furious and immediately sent Yu Dichen, the Director of Education at the Police Training Institute, and Inspectors Liu Renyi and Fan Tianxing, along with Chief Gao, to take over the office by force. When they arrived at the bureau, Liu Zhuomin, seeing the unfavorable situation, hid and refused to appear. Only Liu's wife, Li Rongzhen, was there, making a scene, scolding wildly, even pounding on the table and stamping her feet, uttering constant insults.

Hiding Firearms: Chief Gao and others did not respond but immediately inspected everything in the bureau. Unexpectedly, all the seals and forty-four handguns in the bureau were missing. When they questioned the police officers in the bureau, they all said that Liu Zhuomin had hidden them. Chief Gao and others could not take over the office, so they reported to Director Li again. Li went to the county government and asked County Magistrate Yan for instructions. County Magistrate Yan ordered Chief Gao to handle the affairs first and to send Liu's wife to the county court for questioning if she continued to make trouble unreasonably. After receiving the order, Chief Gao went to take office first, and Ji Yaping, a staff member of the bureau, handed over various documents and files. As for the seals and firearms, they would wait for Liu to hand them over in person.

Arrest of Li Shuyun: Later, Liu Zhuomin received an order from the Civil Affairs Department to arrest him, and his wife, Li Rongzhen, was also arrested and escorted to the Wuxi County Public Security Bureau to be transferred to the Wuxi County Court for interrogation. At the same time, the Civil Affairs Department considered that the mastermind of Liu's case was actually Li Shuyun, the second wife of Civil Affairs Director Gu Renfa. It was discovered that Li had fled to Shanghai with her mother, Mrs. Li (53 years old), and was hiding in the Huang residence at 15 Xinmin Village, Marlborough Road in the French Concession. Director Gu prepared a document, appointing Liu Anxi, the Director of the General Affairs Section of the Civil Affairs Department, and Xu Pucheng, the Chief of the First District of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police, to come to Shanghai on the 20th to report to the French Concession Police and request their assistance in arresting and bringing them back for interrogation.

Apprehending Mother and Daughter: The Detective Chief immediately ordered Chinese and Western detectives to rush to the Huang residence at 15 Xinmin Village, Marlborough Road, and arrest Li Shuyun and her mother, Mrs. Li. A search revealed no evidence of a crime, so they were taken back to the police station. According to Li Shuyun's statement, "Gu Renfa, the Director of the Civil Affairs Department, is my husband. I came to Shanghai from Nanjing on the 13th because I was suffering from stomach problems and sought treatment from Dr. Kong at 419 on the fourth floor of the Continental Emporium. My husband went to Nanchang on the 12th to meet with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. My husband would never denounce me. I know nothing about Liu Zhuomin's refusal to hand over his duties. I know Liu Zhuomin through the introduction of Liu's wife, Wen Rongzhen (not Li Rongzhen), because Liu used to be my husband's subordinate." Mrs. Li stated that she lived at 2 Zhaojia Ping, Changsha, and came with her daughter because she was ill. Based on the statements, the Detective Chief ordered them to be temporarily detained.

Police Opinion: The next day, they were transferred to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court. Judge Li Changnian presided over the hearing. Li Shuyun had cut her hair short and was wearing a coffee-colored silk cheongsam and black satin shoes. After the judge questioned the defendants about their age, origin, and address, Li Shuyun occasionally showed a bitter smile. The police lawyer, Gu Shouxi, then stated the facts of the case, saying that the two defendants were reported to the police by Xu Pucheng, the Chief of the First District of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police, and Liu Anxi, who were from the Civil Affairs Department, as being related to the case of Liu Zhuomin, the Chief of the Second Branch of the Wuxi Public Security Bureau, hiding firearms and seals and refusing to hand over his duties. They requested that detectives be sent to assist in arresting them. However, when the detectives searched the defendants' residence, they found no evidence of a crime. Therefore, according to Article 7 of the Agreement, the police could not extradite them unless the formal court came to transfer them and there was sufficient evidence of the defendants' crimes. Now, the police's opinion is that the staff from the Civil Affairs Department should submit substantial evidence in the near future. Then the police do not oppose it. Moreover, the accuser in this case, Gu Renfa, is the current Civil Affairs Director of Jiangsu Province, also the husband of the first defendant. Since he has a close marital relationship with the defendant, the police should be more cautious.

Request for Transfer: Then, Xu Pucheng and Liu Anxi, the staff from the Civil Affairs Department, submitted an official document, requesting permission to transfer the two defendants back for interrogation. Liu Anxi also said that Li Shuyun was indeed Director Gu's wife and that she was selling official positions and extorting money. This time, Liu Zhuomin's refusal to hand over his duties was orchestrated by her. The Provincial Government had already reported to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and ordered her arrest. However, she took advantage of Gu's trip to Nanchang to meet with Chiang and fled to Shanghai. Therefore, the county magistrate sent them to Shanghai to report to the police for arrest and requested permission for the transfer. Li Shuyun stated that she knew nothing about Liu's case. Subsequently, Zhang Shizhao, Xiang Xun, Tan Xinzhen, and other lawyers hired by the defendants successively expressed their opinions. The court then informed the staff that since Liu's case had been accepted by the Wuxi Court, this case should also be transferred by the Wuxi Court. The case is now being prepared by the Wuxi County Court Procuratorate, which has sent court police Yang Shuzi and Feng Yongbao to Shanghai to receive the transfer from the Second Special District Court this morning. The court immediately notified the police to escort the defendants to the court, where Judge Li opened the Second Criminal Court for trial. First, the police who came presented the official documents, requesting the transfer.

Mother and Daughter Weep Loudly: Then, Gu, the lawyer representing the police, stated that the extradition of criminals by government offices was stipulated in the agreement and requested the court to make a ruling in accordance with the law. When questioned, Li Shuyun stated that she graduated from the Zundao Association School in Changsha. Later, on June 22nd of the 20th year of the Republic of China, she married Gu Renfa, the current Civil Affairs Director of Jiangsu Province, through the introduction of Jin Xiufu. They were married at the Central Hotel in Hankou, with Li Yungong officiating the wedding and Ren Hebin presiding over it. After entering the family, she learned that Gu's ex-wife was still alive and had several children. When she questioned Gu, he said that it was related to his personal reputation and status and told her not to publicize it, saying that he had a way to divorce his ex-wife. Unexpectedly, this has now happened to harm me. I know nothing about Liu Zhuomin's case. The truth is that I have been wronged. After speaking, the mother and daughter covered their faces and wept loudly. Judge Li instructed that this case was a case of assistance and had been accepted by the Wuxi County Court first. The transfer should be approved. The defendant mother and daughter, upon hearing the instruction, cried even louder, saying, "If we are extradited, we fear that our lives will be harmed on the way." The court instructed, "If you have been wronged, the Wuxi County Court will also make a fair judgment and will not make things difficult for you. If you fear that there will be difficulties on the way, this court can send court police to accompany you." After the instruction, the court adjourned and the defendants were taken down to the court police room. The police who came hired a car and drove directly to the North Station to take a train to the Wuxi Court for further trial.

Wang Haiqiu, Who Extorted Ma Zhanshan, Arrested

Wang is Ma's subordinate

The court ordered a retrial at a later date.

General Ma Zhanshan, a famous anti-Japanese general in the Northeast, returned to China via the outer frontiers after running out of ammunition and supplies. After handing over his military seal, he retired in Tianjin. Last month, he suddenly received several threatening letters demanding money. Later, he received a small booklet about Ma Zhanshan, which contained words that damaged Ma's reputation. He then read an advertisement in the Shen Bao on January 28th, stating that "A Small History of Ma Zhanshan" was published by the Asia Translation Agency at 613 Route Lafayette in this city. After a secret investigation, he learned that Wang Changzhi was the person in charge. He then sent a letter to his secretary, You Ju, a native of Wuxian, Jiangsu, to report to the French Concession Police a few days ago, presenting the threatening letters and a booklet, requesting an arrest and investigation. The political department dispatched Western detective Xi Neng (transliteration) and Chinese detective Zhao Zibo, who rushed to 613 Route Lafayette at 8:30 AM the day before yesterday. They saw a wooden sign with the name "Asia Translation Agency" hanging on the door. They entered and searched the premises, which turned out to be a Westerner's residence. They then arrested Wang Haiqiu (32 years old) from Liaoning on the second floor. They confiscated a letter signed by Ma Zhanshan, and a draft, a letter from Du Chongyuan to Du Yuesheng, a letter from Du Chongyuan to Ma Zhanshan, a letter to Ji Qing, and a letter to Ziyuan. They also removed the sign from the door and took it to the police station. Yesterday, they were escorted to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court, where Judge Wang Gangxu presided over the hearing. The police lawyer, Fei Xizhen, stated the facts of the case, saying that the defendant, Wang Haiqiu, was arrested based on a report by General Ma Zhanshan's representative, You Ju, to the police, and letters were confiscated as evidence. The police still need to conduct a detailed investigation and requested a seven-day extension to investigate the case. The evidence was presented to the court. When questioned, Wang Haiqiu stated that the Asia Translation Agency was run by Zhao Jianfeng, and he was the secretary, only responsible for receiving and sending letters and copying manuscripts, with a monthly salary of 30 yuan. He knew nothing about the booklet and threatening letters about Ma Zhanshan. Zhao used to be the director of the military supplies department under General Ma, and he was his old subordinate. Zhao has now left Shanghai for Nanjing, Beiping, or Hankou. The house at 613 Route Lafayette was rented until yesterday and has been returned. Detective Zhao Zibo reported that when they searched, the defendant took the letters from his pocket and threw them under the bed. The letters presented to the court were retrieved. You, the representative of General Ma, stated that General Ma received the letters and booklet in Tianjin. Xiang Xun, the lawyer hired by the defendant, stated that the defendant was currently ill and requested that he be released on bail or sent to a hospital for treatment during the extended period. The police opposed bail because the case was under investigation but requested that the court grant a shorter period. The defendant stated that he was suffering from hematuria and could not be released on bail, requesting permission to be sent to a hospital for treatment. The court approved the request and ordered a retrial on the 28th after the investigation. The defendant was temporarily detained by the police. The court also instructed the police detectives that if the defendant was indeed ill, he could be sent to Guangci Hospital for treatment. After the instruction, the court adjourned and the defendant was taken away by the police for investigation.

Daytime Robbery in Zhuhang Alley, Southern Shanghai, Apprehended

An old man gathered for mahjong, the daughter-in-law opened the door, and thieves entered.

Neighbors heard the commotion and called the police. The two thieves confessed, but their statements diverged.

Shen Jingzhou, 67, from Gaoqiao, Pudong, is the general manager of Yichang Qianzhuang on Huayi Street, outside Dadongmen, Nanshi. He lives at 169 Zhuhang Alley, near the Qianzhuang. Because the Qianzhuang is prosperous and has annual surpluses, Shen's family has accumulated a lot of wealth, the furnishings are luxurious, and life is comfortable, attracting the attention of bandits. Yesterday, after lunch, Shen was bored at home and invited his local co-resident, Xu Lingtao, and others to play mahjong. At 2:35 PM, they suddenly heard a very urgent knock on the door. Shen's daughter-in-law went out to ask who was knocking. She heard someone outside the door say, "I am from Yichang Qianzhuang, sending a note to Mr. Shen." The daughter-in-law thought it was the old clerk from Yichang Qianzhuang and did not suspect anything else, so she opened the door. Unexpectedly, after opening the door, she saw three people standing outside, none of whom were from Yichang Qianzhuang, and their faces were ferocious. Knowing that they were not good people, she quickly tried to close the door, but the three people pushed the door open with force, barged into Shen's house, took out guns, drove Shen's daughter-in-law and Xu Lingtao, who were playing mahjong, to a corner, and forbade them from making any noise. They sternly asked Shen and others, "We are under orders to search for opium." After saying this, they searched Shen's daughter-in-law and took 16 silver dollars from her pocket, putting them into their bags. At this time, Shen and others realized that they were bandits and were all panic-stricken. The bandits left one bandit to watch Shen and others, while two bandits went upstairs straight into the bedroom, overturning boxes and cabinets and looting wildly. Unexpectedly, Shen Dizhuang, a resident of 173, the house next door to Shen's family, heard the commotion and quickly ran out to call the watchmen Zhuang Maojin of the sixth gang and Zhang Quanan of the seventh gang to come and guard the door of Shen's house. At the same time, they used the telephone to report to the First Section of the First District and asked for assistance in the arrest. The section dispatched Inspector Guo Qingchong, leading Sergeants Zhang Fengjun, Zhu Lianqing, Police Officers Zhang Zide, Pu Yongchang, Li Mingyang, Li Jingzhai, Ji Yintang, Detective Yu Maolong, and more than twenty others, all armed, and rushed to the address. They surrounded Shen's house like they were facing a formidable enemy. Passersby on the road did not understand the truth and were greatly frightened, scattering and fleeing in all directions. The bandit who was watching Shen and others had noticed that the police detectives had arrived outside to arrest them. He pretended to be calm, hid the gun in his pocket, opened the door, and walked out slowly, hoping to avoid the eyes and ears of the detectives and police and not be suspected as a bandit. However, the detectives outside the door saw that his clothing was improper and knew that he was not a good person, so they arrested him. The bandit repeatedly stated that he was not a robber. The police searched him and found a Browning pistol with serial number 677 and six bullets. The bandit then lowered his head and was speechless. At that time, Inspector Guo saw that one bandit had already been arrested and led the police detectives to rush into Shen's house, straight up the stairs. They saw one bandit still looting property in the bedroom and rushed forward to arrest him. They found 11 silver dollars and a Browning pistol with serial number 63 and seven bullets on his person. However, one bandit had already escaped and was not captured. The two bandits were taken back to the section. When Section Chief Yi interrogated them, one confessed that his name was Lu Zixiang, 38 years old, from Chongming. This time, the robbery of Shen's house was initiated by Wang Amao, a native of Chuansha, who lived at 8, Lane 2, Runan Lane, opposite the Xiaocai Market in the Zhabei Public Welfare Lane. There were a total of six people who went to commit the robbery, all of whom were invited by Wang. Three people were scattered outside the door to keep watch. Lu Zixiang and Lu Bu'ao, who were arrested at the same time, broke into Shen's house and were arrested by the police. All the guns were also given to them by Wang Amao at the Gongan Inn on Wuma Road at about 9:00 PM last night (the night before last) to be used for the robbery. When questioned, Lu Bu'ao confessed that he was 30 years old, from Haimen. He was also invited by Wang Amao to commit the robbery, but he did not know Wang's residence. He did not know Lu Zixiang before. Last night, he went to the Gongan Inn to discuss the robbery because he was invited by Wang and met Zixiang. He met and knew each other through Wang's introduction. The section then dispatched Squad Leader Dong Mingde, Han Ruisheng, and Detectives Yuan Haishan and Wang Guilin to accompany the bandit Lu Zixiang to Zhabei and, together with the chief police of the First Section of the Fourth District, rushed to Runan Lane. The bandit Lu pointed out and arrested one person and took him back to the section. When the section chief questioned him, the person confessed that his name was Liu Yushan, 47 years old, from Shandong. He had been working as a police officer in the Haining Road Police Station for more than ten years. "I am not Wang Amao, nor am I from Chuansha. I don't know the two bandits, Lu, either. Last night (the night before last) from 6:00 PM to 6:00 AM the next morning, I was assigned to guard a warehouse on Arabasta Road. How could I have had the time to go to the Gongan Inn to conspire with Lu and others to rob Shen's house? Today, I was sitting at home when the detectives came and arrested me, saying that I was a robber. I was really confused, but I don't know why I was falsely accused by the bandit Lu." However, the bandit Lu Zixiang insisted that the person was his accomplice Wang Amao. When questioned, Lu Bu'ao said that the person was definitely not Wang Amao, because he knew Wang well. As to whether Liu Yushan was Wang Amao or was falsely accused by Lu and others with the intention of framing him, further investigation is still needed. An official document was ordered to be prepared and the three captured criminals were sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation this morning.

Sisters Jointly Sue Stepmother

Filing a lawsuit to divide the property.

Shen Xiaomao, a native of this county, started as a farmer and owned a lot of real estate in Shanghai. He first married a woman surnamed Mou, who bore him two daughters, the elder named Xin'e and the younger named Lin'e. After Mou died of illness, Shen remarried a woman surnamed Li, who bore him a son and two daughters. The son, named Fugeng, died young. The two daughters were named Fudi and Meidi. Shen died of illness in 1928, leaving behind real estate including 1.7 acres of land at Minhou North Village, Hartung Road, 1.67 acres of land at Jiangjiajiao, 3 acres of houses and land in Sanjingbang City, Zhoujiaqiao, 1 acre of land at Zhanghongqiao, and 2 acres of land near the Hongqiao Airport, as well as cash, totaling no less than 150,000 yuan, all managed by Li. Last year, when Xin'e married into the Zhou family, Li was perfunctory. She also abused Lin'e in every way, causing Lin'e to be unable to live in peace and to leave home and temporarily live with the Qi family. Xin'e and Lin'e then hired lawyer Che Bingrong to send a letter to Li, seeking a division of property. However, Li kept delaying, and they had no choice but to file a lawsuit with the First Special Court, requesting the entire estate to be divided into five parts in accordance with Articles 1164 and 1138 of the Civil Code, with the plaintiffs receiving two-fifths of the estate. Because they were unable to pay the litigation fees, they requested litigation assistance, which was approved. Yesterday morning, Judge Yu Changzi of the First Special Court opened the Eleventh Civil Court for hearing. The defendant, Shen Li, argued that the entire estate left by Shen Xiaomao was only worth 17,000 yuan, and that it was divided immediately after her husband's death, with each of the two plaintiffs receiving 2,500 yuan. However, the plaintiffs denied this, saying that the defendant had sold a piece of land and obtained more than 10,000 yuan, and the defendant gave them each 500 yuan as funds for other uses. The division of property was purely fictitious. After questioning, the court ordered a postponement for further verification.

A Woman Who Has Been Separated for a Long Time Sues to Confirm the Mother-Son Relationship

Feng Qiting, who was once poor, is now rich.

The woman is unable to support herself and the son should be ordered to provide support.

丨 Feng Admits Cohabitation, Denies Having a Son 丨

Feng Qiting, 53, from Baoding, Hebei Province, has been doing business in this city. In 1914 and 1915, he met a young woman surnamed Yang and began cohabiting with her. After several years, Feng, due to economic difficulties and being unable to provide for her, separated from the woman. Since then, they have been estranged and Yang has found another place to live. For many years, there has been no communication. In recent years, Feng's business has prospered and he has established Hengji Leather Goods Store in Shanjia Garden and is also the manager of a carpet company downstairs at Jinlong Western Restaurant on Tibet Road. Yang, feeling old and facing difficult circumstances, has a haggard face and no one to pity her. She learned that Feng has become rich, which touched her past feelings. She then hired a lawyer and filed a complaint with the First Special District Court, saying that she had a son named Amao when she cohabited with Feng. Later, they separated and the son was taken by Feng to raise. It has been nineteen years now. She is now old and unable to make a living and should be supported by her own son. She requested a judgment confirming that she and Feng Amao have a mother-son relationship. However, Amao is still a minor and Feng Qiting is Amao's legal guardian, so she specifically listed Qiting as a defendant as well, requesting that he be summoned together. Yesterday morning, Judge Luo Chongtai held a trial. Feng Qiting, accompanied by his representative lawyer Jiang Yiping, appeared in court. Lawyer Jiang raised the issue of jurisdiction, saying that Feng Qiting's residence was in his hometown and that his son's name was Xiaomao, not Amao, and that he was also in his hometown and had been adopted by the eldest son. He requested that this issue be resolved first before the content of the case could be heard. The plaintiff's representative lawyer then said that Feng Qiting has been doing business in the Public Concession and his residence is in his leather goods store. Since he is Amao's legal guardian, this case should be under the jurisdiction of this court and there is no question of jurisdiction. Judge Luo then questioned Feng Qiting, who stated that he lived in the countryside of Baoding and had a leather goods store and a carpet company in Shanghai. In 1915, he cohabited with the plaintiff, but Xiaomao was not born to the plaintiff and was adopted by his brother and sister-in-law at the age of twelve with his father's permission. However, according to the plaintiff Feng Yang, she cohabited with Feng in 1915 and gave birth to a son in 1916, named Amao. The midwife was called by Feng, and the landlord Ge Debao knew this very well. She requested that Ge be summoned to court to prove it. Later, Feng had no money and she supplied everything, costing thousands of yuan. Feng took Amao away when he was six years old. In recent years, he was studying at Nanyang School. Feng hid him because she asked for this son. The court ordered a postponement for further investigation as it still needed to be investigated.

Zhabei Charity Group Jointly Provides Congee Relief for Fire Victims

Recently, two major fires occurred in Zhabei, on Pushan Road and Jingjiang Road, burning down hundreds of thatched houses. The victims numbered in the thousands, mostly laborers. The Chinese Red Cross Society and the Xinwei Relief Society distributed rice tickets, silver dollars, and old clothes to the victims. The Chinese Jisheng Association and the Zhabei Charity Group jointly distributed congee, starting on March 13th at Liuying Road, distributing congee with vouchers, three spoonfuls for adults and two spoonfuls for children, requiring more than eleven dan of congee rice per day. Nearly 3,000 people have been given congee for eleven days. The suffering victims were grateful. The emergency relief was quite difficult in terms of financial resources. They are now trying to raise funds.

Excerpts from the Jishēng Hui Meeting Minutes

The China Jishēng Hui moved into its new premises at No. 20 Gùjiānòng, Níngbō Road on February 28th. The first meeting was held the day before yesterday. More than twenty people attended, including Deputy Chairmen Xú Qiánlín and Huáng Hánzhī, and Standing Committee member Zhū Qìchén. Chairman Wáng Yītíng was absent due to illness, so Deputy Chairmen Xú and Huáng presided. The minutes of the previous meeting were read, followed by a report from Director Zhènwù, Mr. So-and-so, regarding joint efforts with the Zháběi Charity Group to provide porridge at two large disaster relief sites on Jīngjiāng Road and Pǔshàn Road in Zháběi; spring relief in Ānhuī's Fùyáng, Yǐngshàng, and Tàihé counties in cooperation with the Huáng Hé Flood Emergency Relief Association; work relief for the Guangfeng embankment and small embankment projects in Jiangxi; porridge distribution at the Chaoyangmen outside Beijing and at the Báiyī'ān porridge factory; grain distribution by the Cháng'ān branch in Shǎnxī; and emergency relief in Fujian in conjunction with the Eight Virtues Association. These efforts require substantial funds, so everyone's attention is requested. Furthermore, Director of Finance, Mr. So-and-so, reported that from January 1st to March 19th of this year, a total of 19,417.55 yuan was received in relief funds, and a total of 13,976.52 yuan was paid out. The Guangfeng embankment project in Jiangxi and the Liǔyíng Road porridge factory in Zháběi still have unpaid relief funds of 5,000-6,000 yuan. Currently, the market is sluggish, and income is not covering expenses. Water disasters are repeatedly occurring in Henan, Hebei, and western Shandong, with suffering people everywhere. With a compassionate heart, we should do everything we can for relief efforts. Last year, more than 17,000 yuan was spent on medicine. Now, in this time when the epidemic has not completely subsided, various places rely on our association's medicine, and its use is becoming more widespread. This year, about 20,000 yuan will be needed for medicine. Please discuss together how to provide relief, and with a sense of conscience, plan for expansion. We should also publicly nominate several comrades with a well-established reputation to serve on our association's standing committee, seeking their guidance and assistance to aid relief efforts. At this time of moral decline and popular demoralization, we should actively promote and attempt to remedy the situation and prevent disasters.

"Taiwan Koala" artificial marble, invented by a German engineering expert, surpasses natural marble in quality. Available in all colors, customers can choose colors and customize their order, ensuring satisfaction. Its quality is solid and durable, never cracking or eroding, even with severe frost and ice, rain, or sun exposure. It maintains its brilliance, and any rubbing or dirt will not fade. Its price is extremely low, making it ideal for modern and economical construction. Because of the advantages listed above, it has been unanimously recognized and widely adopted by the construction industry in Europe and the United States. The Shanghai Far East Marble Co., Ltd. has purchased its manufacturing secrets and established a factory at No. 169, Xīmén Road, French Concession, hiring

specialist engineers to refine and produce it, available for use. The company has exclusive sales rights in China and Southeast Asia, with many samples available. All are welcome to visit and view them.

Meeting of Christian Organizations to Promote Rural Revival

The Commission on the Thrust of Christian Institutions of the National Christian Council of China, located at No. 169 Yuánmíngyuán Road, held a meeting at its offices the other day. Committee members included Mr. Zhào Jìnqīng, Dr. Lǐ Dēnghuī, Mr. Chén Lìtíng, Mr. Chén Zōngliáng, Mr. Zhū Lìdé, etc. After detailed discussion by the attending committee members, they concluded that in this time of rural economic collapse, if the intention is to assist various churches in becoming self-supporting, the first priority should be assisting farmers in various places to improve agricultural products and various side occupations, and to promote cooperatives, in order to achieve the goal of revitalizing the rural economy. However, this matter is extensive in scope and the problems are complex. It has now been decided that further meetings are required to allow for proactive implementation.

The Unprinted National Gazetteer: Jiaqing Revised Unified Gazetteer

The Commercial Press reprints from manuscript.

An important work in the Continued Compilation of the Four Series.

The Qīng Unified Gazetteer was first printed in the ninth year of the Qiánlóng reign, in 356 volumes. It was revised and printed in the 55th year, increasing to 424 volumes. Reduced-size editions of these two books have been available on the market, but the number of volumes has varied, greatly distorting the original appearance of the book. This time, the Commercial Press is reprinting the third revision from the late Qīng dynasty, ending in the 25th year of the Jiāqìng reign, completed in the 22nd year of the Dàoguāng reign. It begins with a catalog in two volumes, followed by 511 volumes covering the capital and various provinces, followed by 34 volumes covering Xinjiang, Mongolia, Tibet, the Western Regions, and dependent territories, plus 11 volumes covering tributary states, totaling 562 volumes. It contains tables of historical changes for each province and department, tables of prefectures, departments, and sub-prefectures, a complete map, provincial maps, maps of prefectures, departments, and sub-prefectures, and maps of various departments. The contents are divided into twenty-five categories: territory, regional divisions, establishment and evolution of administrative divisions, topography, customs, city walls, schools, population, land taxes, tax revenues, official positions, mountains and rivers, historical sites, passes, ferries and bridges, dikes and embankments, mausoleums, ancestral temples, temples and monasteries, famous officials, historical figures, exiles, virtuous women, immortals and monks, and local products. The analysis is meticulous, more detailed than the Qiánlóng revision. Omissions and errors in the original have been corrected. It is the most detailed and comprehensive official gazetteer ever produced. The entire book consists of more than 13,700 leaves. At the time, it was only presented as a manuscript and never printed. The Commercial Press borrowed the original book from the Qing History Museum, photographed it, and is publishing it as part of the first installment of the Continued Compilation of the Four Series, scheduled for publication on April 1st. Due to the large number of volumes, the Wáng Yúnwǔ Four-Corner Number Indexing Method has been used to create an index for ease of reference. It is an essential reference for those studying Chinese geography. It is reported that the complete book consists of 200 volumes, plus 10 index volumes, and is sold separately for 110 yuan per set, 10% discount for cash payment. Those who pre-order the complete set of the first installment of the Continued Compilation of the Four Series, in addition to this book, will also receive 300 volumes of other Song and Yuan editions for a pre-order price of only 150 yuan, an increase of only 51 yuan, an extremely rare opportunity. It is learned that in order to facilitate those who only wish to purchase the Unified Gazetteer, the deadline for pre-ordering the complete set of the first installment of the Continued Compilation of the Four Series has been extended by ten days, to April 10th, and a sample of the Unified Gazetteer has been specially printed for reference.

Ministry of Finance Orders All Banks to Prohibit the Imitation of Banknotes in Gift Certificates

The Ministry of Finance recently stated that the issuance of gift certificates by banks originally served as a type of deposit certificate, facilitating social interactions and gift-giving, which was acceptable. However, the design of some gift certificates printed by various banks resembled banknotes, inevitably creating the suspicion of profiting from counterfeiting. Therefore, the ministry had generally deleted the terms "gift certificates" and "savings" from the registered articles of association of various banks, as a measure to ensure the integrity of certificates and prevent abuses. However, it has been discovered that some banks still issue gift certificates under their savings departments without prior approval, which is improper. Therefore, a special notice has been issued stating that in the future, banks must first submit an application to the ministry for approval before issuing gift certificates. Those that have already issued gift certificates must submit one sample of each type of gift certificate to the ministry for approval within three days of receiving the order, in order to prevent abuses.

Tour of the City God Temple and Yu Garden

Police Station Sends Police for Protection

Total Principal Repaid: 180,000 Silver Dollars

Payments to Begin at the End of This Month

Shanghai Municipal Council Discusses This Year's Finances

The Municipal General Rates Will Remain at 14 Percent

A Shortfall of 1.9 Million Will Be Made Up From the Reserve Fund

At the meeting of the Shanghai Municipal Council on the 21st of this month, the Director of Finance reported that the budget for this year had been largely completed and would be submitted to the Finance Committee for review in the coming days. The most important point for the Council to consider was the issue of the Municipal General Rates. According to the figures compiled, the total expenditure under the regular budget for this year, 1934, is 26,385,000 yuan, while the total estimated income is 24,431,000 yuan, leaving a shortfall of 1,950,000 yuan, equivalent to about two quarters of the revenue from the Municipal General Rates. How to make up for this shortfall of 1.95 million yuan requires urgent consideration. The budgets for 1932 and 1933 both had shortfalls, which were made up from the reserve fund, the former being 1,225,000 taels and the latter reaching 1,500,000 taels. Whether or not to revert to the old Municipal General Rates (16 percent) this year should be carefully considered in light of the current situation in Shanghai. As for properties subject to the rates, since 1931, due to new construction and re-equalization of valuations, their valuation has increased by 16 million yuan. Now that the valuations are largely equalized, the timing of the rate increase depends on the Council's decision. In recent years, due to the sale of the Electricity Department, taxpayers have enjoyed the benefit of reduced rates, but it has been difficult to balance the budget. However, given the obviously difficult general economic situation, it is advisable to adopt a method that can avoid raising rates if possible in a normal year. There are still remaining funds in the General Reserve Fund, and it is proposed to allocate another 2,000,000 yuan, as in the past two years, to make up the shortfall. After allocating 2 million yuan as proposed, the current General Reserve Fund, which is the remainder from the reorganization of the proceeds from the sale of the Electricity Department, will have a remaining balance of about 550,000 yuan. After discussion, the Council deeply felt that the current expenditure of the Municipal Council was actually exceeding the regular income, but was very pleased that there was a way to delay the rate increase for another year and avoid submitting it to the Ratepayers' Annual Meeting this year. The proposal by the Director of Finance to allocate 2 million yuan from the General Reserve Fund to maintain a balanced budget was approved for implementation.

Mechanical Industry Federation Petitions for Increased Import Duties on Rubber Tape

Japanese Goods Dumped, Domestic Inventory Piles Up

The Mechanical Industry Federation of this city, due to the dumping of Japanese rubber tape at low prices, specially petitioned the National Government and the Ministry of Finance yesterday, requesting an increase in import duties and the imposition of anti-dumping duties. The original petition stated: "Regarding the dumping of Japanese rubber tape at low prices, which greatly affects domestic products, we respectfully petition for an increase in import tax rates or the implementation of anti-dumping duties to remedy the situation. We respectfully submit a letter from our member, Shen Yi Rubber Tape Factory, stating that in order to recover lost profits, we first raised funds to establish a factory to manufacture domestic rubber tape. Various Shen Yi brand narrow and wide rubber tapes have already been manufactured, specifically for use in domestic factories' machinery. They have been sold in the market for half a year now and have been well received by the factory sector in various places. We have recently been working hard to improve the manufacturing methods in order to refine and develop them, so as to effectively resist foreign goods.

Unexpectedly, since the products were launched and sold last year, Japanese rubber tape has been sold at low prices, and domestic goods have gradually been affected. Upon investigation, the tax levied on imports from Japan is very low in our country, only 14.25 per 100, which has led to a large number of Japanese rubber tapes coming to China, wielding their ambition of economic aggression and using their harsh tactic of dumping at low prices. For example, Japanese rubber tape is sold for only 1.3 cents per layer per inch when transported and sold in our country. According to its domestic sales price, it should be sold for 2 cents per layer per inch. The cost of domestic rubber tape is 1.5 cents per layer per inch, which is slightly different from the dumping price of Japanese rubber

tape. However, factory fees, etc., have not been added to our factory's products, and promotion has been greatly affected. Inventory is piling up, and the situation is worrying. This kind of dumping behavior is a fatal blow to domestic rubber tape, and the harm to the industry is extremely serious. May we ask, the Earth Brand, Double Deer Brand, Head Brand, etc., listed in hardware and grocery stores such as Beijing Road Mantingfang in Shanghai are all Japanese goods, and the above-mentioned selling prices are still consignment prices. If wholesale in large quantities, the price is even cheaper. If this continues, not only will workers suffer from unemployment, but the only rubber tape factory in Shanghai will be in danger of being unable to recover. Upon investigation, the Japanese government uses military force to invade neighboring countries, and also adopts a policy of economic aggression to support or subsidize its domestic and foreign manufacturing factories in order to compete with our fledgling domestic products. If remedies are not quickly sought, or measures are not taken to ban them, what unimaginable consequences will there be? We have always known that your association has the goal of protecting domestic products and resisting foreign goods, so we have specially listed the situation of enemy goods and sent a letter to request that you submit it to the government for practical guarantees, and instruct the customs to increase the import tax rate on rubber tape, so as to avoid exploitation and benefit domestic goods. The letter states that the selling price of Japanese rubber tape, as stated by the factory, is different domestically and abroad, which shows that there is dumping, and that our country's import tariff is only 14.25 percent, which is too low. It is reasonable to forward the situation as it is, and we respectfully request that your ministry consider and verify whether to impose an anti-dumping tax or increase the import tax rate, in order to remedy the situation and benefit domestic products. We cannot wait to submit this."

Umbrella Factory Workers Oppose Wage Cuts

Yesterday Morning, They Went to the Party Headquarters to Petition

Presenting Five Demands

According to Dakongshe, over a thousand workers from 53 umbrella factories, including Huali Shi in this city, declared a joint work stoppage starting yesterday morning in protest against the factories' wage cuts. They all went to the city's Party Headquarters to petition for assistance. In the afternoon, they convened a general meeting and decided to strike collectively starting today. The five demands presented by the workers are listed below: (1) Limit working hours and maintain jobs for the unemployed. (2) Please restrain the employers from abusing apprentices. (3) Request a letter to the Social Affairs Bureau to promptly resolve the conditions of 1933, fulfilling the original conditions of 1929 before the signing. (4) Request the restoration of original wages. (5) Request that employers not hire non-members and not dismiss workers without cause.

The Rickshaw Trade Association's Special District Office convened its eighth council meeting at 9 PM on March 22nd. Twelve committee members including Zhu Honggao, Qiu Furang, and Liang Ruiting attended. Yin Zhiling was elected as chairman. Mr. Yin reported that the Municipal Council's stance was unbiased and that the buying and selling of licenses was illegal. He stated that he had replied that there was no such occurrence. He also knew that public rickshaw rentals were impossible. They were now backing down and forming a committee of two Chinese and one Westerner to conduct thirteen motions. Issues regarding rickshaw rentals and other matters could be submitted to the committee for negotiation. The rickshaw merchants were very dissatisfied with the rickshaw rentals and intended to adopt the office's advice to reach a compromise without being biased. The preparatory meeting today should discuss and pass various motions. The following was discussed: (1) Discussion on how to remedy the situation now that there is no contractor for public rickshaw rentals and the rickshaw merchants are also not benefiting. It was resolved to submit the issue of any obstacles to rickshaw rentals for discussion at the general meeting. (2) Discussion on the selection of members for the rickshaw committee that the Municipal Council now needs to form. It was resolved to request that the Municipal Council understand the situations of rickshaw merchants, owners, contractors, and pullers when selecting members and consider the suggestions provided by the rickshaw industry. This should be passed at the general meeting. (3) Discussion on the council's nomination of committees for the construction of a hospital and new village. It was resolved to pass it at the general meeting. (4) Discussion on the progress of the building project and urging payments according to the resolutions of the previous rickshaw owners' meeting. The following was resolved: A. A fee of five dollars per rickshaw should be collected, starting from April 1st, and the finance section should negotiate with the bank to collect it in one lump sum. B. The collected fees should be remitted by the finance section to the bank for safekeeping and passed at the general meeting. C. The appointment of a custodian committee and the specification of payment methods should be decided at the general meeting. The meeting adjourned at 11:30 PM after the discussions.

Customers have been pouring in for days, and business is booming. The scattered silks and satins in the bureau's display windows have been mostly cleared. All the bulk silk goods stored in the warehouse have also been dyed in fashionable colors and are now being sorted out. The second phase of the clearance sale will begin tomorrow. It is said that the bureau is determined to clear out the entire inventory, leaving not an inch behind, and the prices have been reduced again. Plain and patterned real wool gabardine is selling for only six dimes and eight cents per foot, less than one-sixth of the original purchase price. According to a bureau employee, the reason is that it is inconvenient to transfer the inventory during the reorganization into a national goods company, and time is very short, so they have no choice but to ignore the losses in order to clear the inventory as soon as possible.

Reading Q&A

How to Study the Northeast Issue (4)

Yesterday, this column provided a general discussion of the overall method for this issue. Today, we will continue with a concrete examination, starting with the first set of opposing factors. Editor

First, let us start by examining the first set of opposing factors.

The opposition between imperialist powers has become increasingly blatant since the world economic crisis began in 1929. As the crisis deepened, the field of struggle expanded universally and became white-hot. This struggle is reflected in the Northeast in the form of two lines of struggle: one line is led by Japan, which seeks to monopolize the interests of Manchuria, and the other line is led by the United States, which seeks to maintain the "Open Door Policy" and "territorial integrity." The attitude of the League of Nations countries (excluding Japan, of course) at that time was also in favor of the latter, as it was deemed more advantageous. As for the other imperialist powers, they had fewer interests at stake, and their opinions ultimately could not become the main ones, so we will not discuss them for the time being. The outbreak of this struggle was naturally inevitable, but its outbreak in 1930 was entirely due to the economic crisis and the political crisis it spawned, which provided a new stimulus for the Japanese financial bourgeoisie (I say financial bourgeoisie rather than Japanese militarists because the Japanese militarists are merely tools of the financial bourgeoisie; the Japanese military is acting on the orders of these financial magnates) to use colonial aggression wars to resolve the domestic economic crisis and alleviate the political crisis. At that time, the overall relationship between international imperialist powers was also undergoing a comprehensive shift and disintegration from relative equilibrium due to the deepening of the crisis, which gave Japan a superior position. Thus, Japan used the call for anti-Sovietism (which will be discussed in detail below), and the "September 18th Incident" was born as a result.

This change naturally alarmed the entire world. It was the beginning of a reorganization of the forces of imperialism in the Pacific and the signal for World War II.

Looking back at the development of this set of opposing factors over the past three years, we can already see that Japan, at least on its part, has achieved a breakthrough in the past equilibrium and shattered the "joint management" line of the United States and the League of Nations. Until recently, the facts have shown that Japan's line has been developing throughout the entire territory of China, and the League of Nations itself has produced Japan's line. For example, following Manchuria, there was the autonomy of Inner Mongolia, the independence of southern Xinjiang, the occupation of the Nine Islands, the invasion of Tibetan troops, the seizure of Yunnan mines, etc., which indicates a shift from the joint management line to a line of partition. The recent establishment of a new understanding between the United States and Japan cannot be regarded as accidental. It is merely a manifestation of the development of this set of opposing factors in the Far East, along with the ebb and flow of the international struggle led by the two powers of Britain and the United States. If the Ten-Nation Conference on the Pacific can truly be successfully convened next year, then that may be the complete victory of Japan's line (implementing the partition of China), but it is not Japan's victory. What follows is a war of division that will inevitably break out as a result of this line, and the result will still be war. Although we are not as bold as the British writer Wells in making some pointless predictions to scare people, the Northeast issue cannot be separated from the development of this set of opposing factors, and we dare to say with certainty that we have grasped the development trend of this set of opposing factors.

Many upper-class Chinese, seeing this set of opposing factors, develop a mentality of relying on the League of Nations or the United States, wanting to play the old trick of "using barbarians to control barbarians," and still wanting to restore the emasculated equilibrium. When things do not go as they wish, they fantasize about "same race and same culture" and "Pan-Asianism," completely recognizing thieves as fathers. In addition, many enthusiastic young people, seeing Japan's management of Manchuria, weep and lament that "the hearts of the people will be lost" and that "the Northeast will be impossible to recover in ten years." This is all because they do not understand the development of this set of opposing factors in a dynamic way, or they only see temporary phenomena and mistakenly believe that they are unchanging, or they see Japan's temporary prosperity in managing Manchuria in isolation, forgetting that the world economic crisis is ubiquitous and that Manchuria, even if it is temporarily prosperous, cannot be an exception. Moreover, how can Japan make Manchuria prosperous at present? Didn't Mr. Fang say "poisoning policy"? What is the basis of this "poisoning policy"? We cannot agree with the opinion implied by Mr. Fang that it is entirely based on the ethical concept of national slaughter. It is clearly a kind of abnormal production under the economic crisis after the bankruptcy of colonial agriculture. Japan clearly cannot save Manchuria from the economic crisis (especially the agricultural crisis), just as it cannot resolve the crisis in its own country. Japan's agricultural products are already in surplus, and it will never allow Manchuria's agriculture to develop regularly. Therefore, there is the act of forcing farmers to grow tobacco. This is by no means defending Japan. This is to say that if the world market needs wheat and soybeans at this time, Japanese capitalists will never forget this normal and profitable production and engage in this immoral business. In the "business经" of merchants, making a profit is clearly the only principle. The so-called national hatred, if separated from the plunder of "wealth," Japanese capitalists would probably feel meaningless! This nakedly exposes the bankruptcy of the rural areas of Northeast China, Japan's inability to prosper the Northeast, Japan's inability to save the Northeast from jumping out of the crisis, and the daily deterioration of the lives of the people in the Northeast. What is lurking here is the spark of resistance that will be ignited by the desire for survival, not submission to Japan and forgetting China. At the same time, this fate is not determined by Japan; it is the inevitable fruit of the capitalist system. Therefore, Mr. Fang's worries, although stemming from patriotism, have become harmful pessimism because he removed other factors when observing.

There are also many observers who can generally grasp the principles of this set of opposing factors, but do not want to incorporate new events that are changing in order to absorb new materials and enrich the content of their research. For example, everyone seems a little excited about the recent reform of the Manchurian state, but they are silent about the independence of southern Xinjiang and the autonomy of Mongolia. Their understanding of the national crisis is limited to the "September 18th Incident" stage and cannot link these new events of the same essence together to recognize the seriousness of the "Northeast Incident" in these new events.

In short: This set of opposing factors is still developing. Before the expansion and victory of the Chinese national liberation war, it still has a decisive effect on the Northeast issue, and we still deserve to pay attention to it from time to time. (To be continued)

Education News from Other Cities

Ministry of Education Commissioners Inspect the Three Colleges of Peiping University

College of Engineering, College of Science, College of Law

(Special Dispatch from Peiping) Today (the 21st), the Ministry of Education inspection commissioners continued to inspect the various colleges of Peiping University. In the morning, they set off in two groups, A and B. Group A, consisting of inspection commissioners Guo Youshou, Chen Kezhong, Liu Yingshi, and Hao Gengsheng, inspected the College of Engineering. Group B, consisting of inspection commissioners Sun Guofeng and Zhou Tianfang, simultaneously inspected the College of Agriculture. In the afternoon, the six commissioners Guo, Chen, Liu, Hao, Sun, and Zhou went to the College of Law for inspection. The details of each inspection are recorded below.

Inspection of the College of Engineering The Ministry of Education inspection commissioners Guo Youshou, Chen Kezhong, Liu Yingshi, and Hao Gengsheng went to the College of Engineering for inspection at 8:30 AM today. Xu Songming, acting president of Peiping University, accompanied them. Zhang Yihui, president of the College of Engineering, and Gu Zhengrong, secretary, received them. First, they inspected the student dormitories, then the classrooms of each department, and then the four factories of electrical engineering, chemistry, mechanical engineering, and textile engineering. The department heads and professors explained everything. Finally, they examined the six departments of registration, documents, general affairs, library, instruments, and dining hall. Hao Gengsheng inspected the physical education situation. They left the college around 12 noon.

Inspection of the College of Agriculture The Ministry of Education commissioners Sun Guofeng and Zhou Tianfang went to the College of Agriculture at 9 AM today, and were received by Liu Yunchou, president of the college, and Ma Chaohan, secretary. They successively inspected the classes of the five departments of agronomy, forestry, agricultural biology, agricultural chemistry, and agricultural economics, and visited the forest farm, but did not visit the agricultural farm. Finally, they inspected the five departments of documents, registration, library, accounting, and general affairs. They left the college around 12 noon.

Inspection of the College of Law The Ministry of Education commissioners Zhou Tianfang, Sun Guofeng, Guo Youshou, Wei Kezhong, Liu Yingshi, and Hao Gengsheng went to the College of Law together at 3 PM yesterday, accompanied by Xu Songming, acting president of Peiping University. Bai Pengfei, president of the college, Deng Bocui, secretary, and professors Liu Shichuan and Li Guangzhong received them. First, they inspected the classrooms of the First College, then the library, research room, and the departments of documents, registration, general affairs, accounting, and dining hall. At 4:10 PM, they inspected the classrooms of the Second College. At 5 PM, they inspected the classrooms of the Third College. At 5:20 PM, they returned to the First College. Each inspection commissioner spoke with Bai Pengfei, president of the college, and others. They left the college at 5:45 PM.

Questions Regarding the Inspection Period Except for Guo Youshou and Sun Guofeng, who are officials of the Ministry of Education, the other commissioners are externally hired. As of today, all six colleges of Peiping University have been inspected. They plan to complete the inspection of all colleges and universities in Peiping before the end of this month. As for the degree of progress made by the various colleges of Peiping University after the reorganization, since the six commissioners had not inspected them before, it is not easy to compare at this moment. However, according to insiders familiar with Peiping University, Peiping University has been on the right track for the past six months.

Ministry of Education Explains the Scope and Organizational Law of Graduation Exams

The Ministry of Education, based on the Shanghai Medical College's request for clarification regarding the scope of graduation examinations and their organizational methods, specifically instructed the college, stating that the organizational methods for the Graduation Examination Committee had already been clearly outlined in the Ministry's Order No. 13328 of the previous year. As for the scope of the graduation examinations, they should be conducted in accordance with Article 17, Paragraph 2 of the University Regulations (the graduation examination is the final semester examination, but the subjects examined must be more than four, with at least two covering the entire academic year). However, the medical college's duration of study is five years, and an internship of one year is required after completion. The "final semester" here refers to the final semester of the fifth academic year. Formal graduation reports for students should be submitted after the completion of the internship. This is for your information.

Sino-Belgian Boxer Indemnity Committee

Requests for Subsidies from All Parties Cannot Be Met Due to Lack of Funds

The Sino-Belgian Boxer Indemnity Committee held a standing committee meeting at 10:00 AM yesterday, the 12th meeting of the Chinese delegation at 11:00 AM, and a joint Sino-Belgian conference at 2:00 PM in the afternoon. The details of the meeting are recorded below.

Attending Committee Members: From the Chinese side, Chairman Chu Minyi, Vice Chairman Zeng Zongjian, Committee Members Li Zhaoshuai, Zhu Shiquan, Kong Lihang, Cai Hong; Attending Secretaries Liu Xichang, Nong Ruhui, Tian Shoucheng; Accountant Pan Zhaobang. From the Belgian side, Chairman Lang Peian, Vice Chairman Le Garre, Committee Members Aelles, Bu Song, and Teflan Shuier; Attending Secretary Lan Bo; Chairman Lang Peian.

Meeting Details: (A) Reporting Items: (1) The Chinese delegation reported on the work situation in the 22nd year; (2) Belgian Committee Member Aelles reported on the process of handling overseas study affairs in Belgium; (3) Committee Member Kong Lihang reported on the situation of inspecting students studying in Belgium; (4) Report of the Sino-Belgian Sanatorium; (5) Accountant Pan reported on the accounts. (B) Discussion Items: (1) The Executive Yuan Secretariat sent a letter requesting the compilation of a budget and attending a joint meeting of Boxer Indemnity agencies. It was resolved to recommend Committee Members Zhu Shiquan and Kong Lihang to attend; (2) University Thesis Award Fund: it was resolved to continue holding the event with the remaining funds of 1,300 yuan from last year's award fund; (3) Unpaid debts of the Beijing-Hankou Railway and Lincheng Coal Mine Company: it was resolved that the General Assembly would send a letter to demand payment; (4) Belgian Committee Member Aelles proposed that studying in Belgium must first be reviewed by the committee, which was resolved and passed; (5) Various requests for subsidies: the Sino-Belgian delegations received dozens of requests for subsidies from all parties, but the committee's large share of funds had already been fully allocated. Currently, only a small amount of funds are available each year, which, in addition to the operating expenses of the two delegations, leaves very little. Therefore, it is impossible to allocate them. The Belgian committee members believe that the institutions previously subsidized by the Chinese delegation do not entirely belong to the Sino-Belgian nature. Therefore, this review of each case is extremely serious, but in reality, there are no funds available for subsidies. There are two reasons for this: firstly, the committee's funds are decreasing year by year, and secondly, due to the impact of the depreciation of the US dollar. Therefore, it is necessary to decline all requests. The General Assembly adjourned at 4:00 PM.

Ministry of Education Approves Record-Keeping of the Shanghai Education Bureau's Measures for Supervising the Enrollment of Secondary Schools

The Shanghai Education Bureau believes that the enrollment of various schools must go through entrance examinations, which is originally to examine whether students have the appropriate academic ability, and is of utmost importance. In order to strictly supervise, it has established ten articles of the "Provisional Measures for the Shanghai Education Bureau's Supervision of Secondary School Enrollment" and submitted them to the Ministry of Education for review. The Ministry of Education added "or Director of Guidance" after the "Director of Academic Affairs," and agreed with the rest. Approval has been granted for record-keeping. The articles of the measures are recorded below:

(1) All secondary schools in this city (hereinafter referred to as "all schools") shall comply with these measures for each enrollment.

(2) For each enrollment, all schools shall conduct entrance examinations for both new and transfer students. During the examinations, physical examinations, written tests, and oral tests shall be conducted separately.

(3) Each school shall conduct entrance examinations no more than three times per enrollment and shall not conduct examinations upon arrival.

(4) Each school shall, ten days before the entrance examination, fill out and submit the enrollment report form formulated by the Bureau to the Bureau.

(5) Each school shall prepare its own entrance examination schedule, fill in the examination subjects and times separately, and submit it to the Bureau at the same time as the enrollment report form.

(6) The Bureau may temporarily send personnel to supervise the entrance examinations of each school.

(7) The Bureau may at any time conduct spot checks and retrieve examination papers from each school.

(8) Within ten days after the completion of all entrance examinations of each school, a student entrance examination grade report shall be filled out and submitted to the Bureau in accordance with the entrance examination process report form formulated by the Bureau.

(9) These measures may be amended at any time if there are any matters not covered.

(10) These measures shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

China Education Construction Society Devotes Itself to Rural Production Enterprises

Overview of the Work of the Huangdu Chicken Farm in the Past Year

The China Education Construction Society has been devoted to production education enterprises in recent years and has achieved considerable results. In the spring of last year, the Society and the Jiangsu Provincial Huangdu Rural Normal School jointly established the Huangdu Chicken Farm, with the aim of improving our country's chicken breeds to increase the auxiliary production of rural areas. Since its establishment, it has been less than a year, and the results have been remarkable. The current situation of the farm is briefly described below for the reference of those engaged in rural production education.

Current Chicken Breeds: In February last year, the farm rented more than ten mu of farmland from the Huangdu Rural Normal School farm as a site, and then started construction of four new-style large and small chicken houses, purchased incubators and brooders, as well as other chicken-raising equipment. In March, it began to hatch and breed chicks, and the results were excellent. There are currently more than 200 white Leghorn hens, which began laying eggs in November last year.

Breeding Work: Currently, the farm is working hard on breeding. In October last year, 50 excellent hens were selected and began to be used in caged nests to record their yields from November 1. It has been four months since then, and it is reported that the average yield of each hen can exceed 80%, and the feathers are beautiful and the chicken bodies are strong, which are truly rare breeding males. In addition, the farm has also retained more than ten strong males, weighing about five catties or more, which are quite in line with the standards of breeding males. In January of this year, the pair mating method (MatinginPairs) was adopted for group mating, and it has been more than two months since then. More than 20 high-quality breeding eggs can be retained every day. In addition to self-sufficiency, there is a slight surplus, and there are many overseas letters ordering them, so the supply is often unable to meet the demand.

Actively Expanding: The farm has been established for a very short time, but it already has a considerable foundation. This year, it is still actively expanding, increasing the number of hens by 500 in preparation for promoting chicken breeds. Three new chicken houses are under construction and will be completed soon. The first hatching began on March 6, and chicks can be bred before the Spring Festival.

Recruiting Student Workers: The farm recently felt that there was a lack of chicken-raising technical talents in the country, so it specially recruited student workers so that they could learn chicken-raising knowledge and skills within a year to meet the needs of society. It is reported that student workers at the four farms, in addition to providing their own meals and paying a deposit of 100 yuan, do not charge other fees. One student has already been recruited, a graduate of Shanghai Middle School in Jiangsu Province, who entered the farm to study in early February.

Settlement of Dispute at Anglo-American Workers' Children School

Party and Government Agencies Mediate, Factory Has Acknowledged

The Shanghai Private Anglo-American Workers' Children School previously had a dispute due to the factory's destruction of labor education. The Fifth District Tobacco Industry Trade Union, based on a resolution of the representative meeting, sent a letter to the Anglo-American Tobacco Company, setting a time limit for a concrete reply, otherwise all employees would strike. At the same time, the school board resolved to determine regular expenses of 1,150 yuan, additional class fees of 400 yuan, and book fees of 300 yuan. The factory representative firmly refused to acknowledge this. The trade union sent representatives Chen Peide and Lou Jingguan to the Municipal Party Department, the Municipal Government Education Bureau, and the Social Bureau to petition separately. The details have been repeatedly reported in previous newspapers. Now it is learned that the dispute at the school has been resolved through the persuasion of party and government agencies, ordering the factory to accept all 900-plus students who have registered this year, increasing regular expenses to 1,050 yuan according to the original amount, adding two classrooms, with the factory providing school supplies and books worth 300 yuan, which the factory will pay as usual. The factory has also acknowledged this and sent a letter of apology to the trade union. The dispute has come to an end.

Sports News

Middle-Distance Running Star Wang Mingshen Arrives in Beiping from the Northeast

Still Full of Spirit, Unwilling to Be a Second-Class Slave of a Fallen Nation

Will Continue to Practice in Preparation for Attending the Far East Games

(Beiping Correspondence) Wang Mingshen, a middle-distance running athlete who has been famous in the Chinese track and field world for several years, has not been heard from in the interior since the Northeast Incident. Yesterday, Wang suddenly arrived in Ping from Harbin by train and stayed at the Northeast Sports Association. The reporter made a special visit. According to Wang,
