Shen Bao Radio Weekly Special Issue on AC Radios (Continued)

Design of Power Transformers

— Ming Sang

The first step in designing a power transformer for a radio is to calculate the power consumed by the radio, which is the product of the voltage and current required for each electrode of the vacuum tubes, with the unit being watts. The transformer itself loses a small portion of power due to resistance and magnetic leakage, so the input power is always greater than the output power. The percentage of input to output

ratio is the efficiency of the transformer.

After knowing the power, the second step is to choose a suitable iron core. Transformer iron cores are made of very thin silicon steel sheets stacked together to prevent eddy current losses. The magnetic field density is standardized at 50,000 to 60,000 lines of magnetic force per square inch. The size of the iron core is usually calculated by the cross-sectional area of the coil. The appropriate size can be found in the fourth row of Table 2.

Table 1

Current 1.7A 1.1 .68 .43 .27 .17 .11 .067 .042 .026 .017

Wire No. 16 18 20 22 24 26 28 30 32 34 36

Table 2

Core Area (Square Inches) I I.14 I.25 I.36 I.50 I.70 I.78 I.90 2.2

Turns per Volt 6.4 5.5 4.8 4.4 4.1 3.75 3.33 3.1 2.84

Efficiency 70% 75% 75% 75% 80% 85% 90% 90% 90%

Input Power (Watts) 30 40 50 60 70 80 100 120 150

The third step is to calculate the current load of each coil

, and determine the appropriate thickness of the wire. Each ampere of current should have a cross-sectional area of I500 circular mils of wire to be safe. The copper wire number and the limit of the current that can be loaded are shown in Table 1. The best material for the wire is enamel-coated copper wire because it has excellent insulation, can withstand high voltage, and is economical and inexpensive.

Finally, the number of turns must be calculated. First, find the number of turns per volt in the third row of Table 2, and then multiply each primary and secondary coil by the required voltage. This is the correct number of turns. Here is another example to clarify the design steps.

The transformer shown in the figure is prepared for a four-tube radio. The secondary coil has three coils: A is used to heat the filaments of two 224 and one 247 vacuum tubes, B is used to heat the filament of the 280 rectifier tube, and C is the high-voltage coil to connect the two plate electrodes of the rectifier tube. According to the vacuum tube characteristics table, the voltage of A should be 2.5V, the current is 31.75 = 5.25Amp, and the power is 2.5V5.25A = 13.12W. B should be 5V2A = 10W. Only the voltage from one end to the center tap needs to be calculated, which is 350V. Assuming the current is 0.05A, then the power is 350.05 = 17.5W. The total power of the transformer is about 40W. In the second row of Table 2, the efficiency is found to be 75% =, so the input power should be 55W. If the primary is 220V, then the current is .25A. The size of the iron core can be found in the last row of Table 2, and the area should be 1.30 square inches. The wire number can be found in Table 1 according to the current required for each coil. The primary should use No. 24 wire, A can use three No. 16 wires wound in parallel, B can use No. 16 wire, and C can use No. 31 wire. Then, from the third row of Table 2, the number of turns per volt is found to be 4.6, so the number of secondary turns should be A2.54.6 = 11.5B = 54.6 = 23C7004.65220. A center tap is connected at 2610 turns, and the number of primary turns is also calculated by the same method 2204.6 = 1012

Transformerless Power Supply

— Wei Xin Su

In the power supply section of an AC radio, the transformer is the most expensive and troublesome component, and the transformer itself is bulky, occupies space, and prevents DC current from passing through. Therefore, designers of AC/DC dual-purpose machines always think of ways to eliminate it. In recent years, with the popularity of small radios, the demand to abandon transformers has become even more urgent.

Removing the transformer is less of a problem in the B voltage aspect, and can be directly supplied with 110V commercial power; as for the low-voltage filament aspect, if relying entirely on resistance reduction, the loss is inevitable. Therefore, new vacuum tubes such as 丨43, 25Z5 with 25V filaments have emerged.

Figure 1

<]

The transformerless power supply device for these new vacuum tubes can be understood by looking at Figure 1. One end of the AC input is connected to the plate electrode of the rectifier tube, and also connected to the filament electrode of the vacuum tube connected in series. The other end is connected to the filament circuit. The current after rectification is output from the cathode.

As shown in Figure 1, the filament electrodes of the three tubes are connected in series, and a resistor R is used to help reduce the voltage. The value of R can be calculated by the following formula.

Resistance in ohms = Voltage supplied 丨 Sum of voltages of each vacuum tube / Current required for vacuum tube filament

Figure 2

<]

For example, in Figure 1, the -77 filament electrode is 6.3V, and both .43 and 25Z5 are 25V, totaling 56.3V. Now, if a voltage of 110V is supplied, subtracting 56.3V leaves 53.7V. The filament current of the above three tubes is all 0.3 amps. Dividing 53.7 by 0.3 gives 179 ohms, which is the value required for the filament. In this device, we must pay attention to making the current passing through each tube equal. As shown in Figure 2, -57 and -57 are both 1.0 amps, while -43 and 25Z5 are only 0.3 amps, with a difference of 0.7 amps, so a resistor R1 must be connected in parallel to make up this 0.7 amps. The value of 0R1 can be obtained by Ohm's law: Required voltage / Voltage to be passed. The filament voltage of -43 and 25Z5 is 50V in total. Dividing 50 by 0.7 equals 71 ohms, which is the value of R1.

For radios using transformerless power supply devices, the grounding point must be strictly isolated with a capacitor, and the connection point of the antenna is best isolated with a capacitor to prevent accidents if the antenna touches the ground.

Filter Circuit for Rectified Power Supply

— Chong Ling

In order to be suitable for AC power, AC radios must have the following three components: (1) transformer, (2) rectifier, and (3) filter. Low-voltage 110 or 220 volt AC power is stepped up to an appropriate high voltage by a transformer, output through a rectifier tube, and converted into pulsating voltage. Therefore, the output current is a pulsating current, and its pulsating frequency is the low frequency of the power supply (50 or 60 cycles per second). If this low frequency or its multiple frequency current is picked up by a low-frequency transformer or directly by a speaker, the AC hum will be noisy. The filter circuit of the rectified power supply is to eliminate the AC hum in the speaker. Therefore, every AC radio must have a filter for the rectified power supply. The pulsating current after rectification is input into this filter circuit, and after the smoothing action of this filter, the output voltage is DC voltage, and the AC voltage component is very small, often only one thousandth of the DC voltage.

The filter circuit is nothing more than a choke coil and a fixed capacitor. The choke coil is naturally a low-frequency iron core choke coil, with a value of 10 to 50 Henrys being suitable. Its function is to smooth the pulsating current. In other words, it prevents the pulsation of the current, because the choke coil has inductance. When the current increases, it will generate a back voltage due to induction to prevent its increase, and when it decreases, it will also cause positive electricity

Figure 1

<]

pressure to prevent its decrease. The capacitor used should also have a large capacitance of 2 to 8 microfarads (mtd). The function of the capacitor is to prevent the pulsation of the voltage and maintain the constant pressure of the output; when the voltage increases, the capacitor is charged, and when the voltage decreases, the capacitor discharges to the end to increase

Figure 2

<]

its voltage, so the pulsating voltage can be converted into a constant pressure output.

Figure 3

<]

There are many types of filter circuits, which vary depending on the arrangement of the choke coil and capacitor. Usually, the types shown in Figure 1, Figure 2, and Figure 3 are commonly used, especially Figure 3 is the best. Figure 2 adds a capacitor to the filter circuit of Figure 1 to smooth the remaining pulsating voltage of the Figure 1 circuit; Figure 3 is a combination of Figure 1 and Figure 2, and most of the better radios use this type. L can use 30 or 50 Henrys, L1 can use 10 or 15 Henrys, and L1L2 can use 30 Henrys low-frequency choke coils; if the output voltage is not high, C, C1, C2, and C3 can use 8 microfarads, otherwise use 2 or 4 microfarads. The current diagram on each figure shows the situation of the pulsating current input being converted into DC output through the filter circuit.

Special Rectifier Device

— Wei Xin Su

The rectifiers used in AC radios can be generally divided into three types: electrolytic rectifier, dry metal disc rectifier, and vacuum tube rectifier. The first type is too cumbersome and inconvenient to use, so very few people use it. The second type is not yet available in Shanghai radio material stores. The third type requires vacuum tubes and transformers, which is quite expensive, and it is not cost-effective to use it to supply a single-tube machine.

In addition to the above three types of rectifiers, we now have a special rectifier. We have long known that electrolytic capacitors have the characteristic of only allowing current to flow in one direction. If an electrolytic capacitor is used in an AC circuit, it cannot condense chemical gas to form a thin film on the anode surface to block the passage of current. By using these two characteristics, an electrolytic capacitor can be used as a rectifier as shown in the figure. C in the figure is a double-connected dry electrolytic capacitor, with 4 MFOCH on each side. H are two 20 Henry choke coils. R2 is a 0-25000 ohm variable resistor. T is a 2.5V small square shed, L is an ordinary three-turn coil, C1 is a 0.0005MF variable capacitor. C2 is a 0.00025MF capacitor, R1 is a 2MEG grid leak resistor. Vacuum tubes such as 157 or -24 can be used.

Analysis of AC Radio Power Supply (Continued)

— Meng Ji

(4) Potentiometer After obtaining a fixed value of voltage, it can be directly applied. However, since the plate and grid of each vacuum tube in the radio require different voltages, potentiometers are also indispensable. A potentiometer is a quantitative resistor. Its two ends are directly connected to the positive and negative poles, and there are also many connections in the middle to supply different voltages. Therefore, the voltage on the detector tube, amplifier tube, and power amplifier tube can be freely selected. The negative voltage on the grid is also mostly taken from the same potentiometer, because positive and negative are originally relative terms. Assuming that the voltage at a certain point on the potentiometer is taken as zero value, then the voltage that is higher than that point is taken as positive, and the voltage that is lower than that point is negative.

Now, the functions and order of the four parts are shown in a diagram. Readers can refer to the diagram to understand the relationship between each part more clearly. The upper part of the diagram shows the order of connection of each part, the lower part shows the function of each part, AB is the reference line, which also indicates the zero potential. Each section of the curve is explained in the diagram below. The shape of the pulsating voltage shown below the rectifier indicates that a full-wave rectifier is used, which makes the two half-cycles of the AC voltage effective. If it is a half-wave rectifier, then only half of the AC cycle is effective, and the other half is cut off and loses its effectiveness. AB is also a reference line, and the waveform curve on the line indicates the shape of the AC filament voltage coming out of the transformer.

Rectifier Circuit

— Zhu Ziyuan

The B voltage in our radio must always use DC. In an AC machine, although the power source is taken from AC, its B voltage is still DC converted from AC, because if we add AC, which changes between positive and negative dozens of times per second, to the plate of the vacuum tube in the radio, there must be a huge AC hum, which completely covers up the sound we want to listen to. Therefore, rectification is very important in AC machines.

After AC passes through rectification, it becomes pulsating DC. If it is used for charging, then it can be charged into a battery, but if it is used as a substitute for B voltage, it must still pass through a filtering device to convert the pulsating DC into pure

Pure DC, and then apply it to the radio, because if this pulsating DC is used to the vacuum tube of the radio, there is still a huge buzzing sound, and

Covering up the required sound, the so-called filtering device is composed of a low-frequency choke coil and a large number of capacitors. This magazine has another article "Filtering Circuit" to explain it in detail, which is omitted here. (To be continued)

Flow Output Current Amperes

Peak Voltage of Output Voltage (Peak Voltage) One Thousand Four Hundred Volts

Essays

All Vehicles Keep to the Left

— Sun Yucai

On the roads of Shanghai, we can see the words "All vehicles keep to the left." It is the same in foreign countries. Next to the roads in London, it is written "Keep the left."

Even the ignorant rickshaw pullers will not pull the rickshaw on the right side of the road, because they know what the consequences will be. They will always remember "All vehicles keep to the left."

If a vehicle does not follow this rule and travels on the right side of the road, a very unfortunate result will immediately occur, completely disrupting the traffic on a road and even the entire city.

Therefore, vehicles must keep to the left to avoid unfortunate events. People know the rules for driving and walking and can abide by them; however, they are completely wrong about things other than the prescribed driving and walking.

They often crash their cars together, causing bloodshed; they would rather not move than yield to the left.

Therefore, British Professor Keynes scolded: "...The world's depression is entirely caused by the world's stubborn and inferior nature. It is like two drivers colliding on the avenue, insisting on not giving way to each other..."

In fact, all the unrest in the world is caused by the stubborn and inferior nature of people in the world, and it is not limited to depression. When this inferior nature is manifested in politics, its impact is self-evident.

If this inferior nature is not removed, China will hardly have a unified destiny.

A Smart Child?

— Fei Pengruo

It is a mother's nature to like her child to be smart. When she expresses her affection to others by saying how smart her child is; this can be said to be the most "true" emotional expression between people in the world.

Mrs. Someone has five children, three boys and two girls. The oldest girl is only six years old. Mrs. Someone likes this child the most because she is the smartest. The reason why this child is smart is that it fits Mrs. Someone's temperament, and only Mrs. Someone can recognize this "smart" as smart. Others may deny it.

The child's name is "Tao Xi." People are a little suspicious of this name. But in Mrs. Someone's own heart, she is very confident that this name is the most meaningful, and it often reminds her of her past pride. She once said to others: "A few days before the child was about to be born, it was a great day. The second landlord's wife 'Teacher Li' hosted a 'betrothal' for her son. Mrs. Someone was invited there to drink. After the banquet, the ladies present gathered together to play a game of 'Mahjong' with a ten-dollar bottom. At the end of nine rounds, Mrs. Someone won three bottoms plus another. This was an unprecedented stroke of luck for Mrs. Someone since she started gambling, and she had never been so happy. Moreover, she had smooth sailing from then on. The first, second, third... few days were also consecutive victories. Unexpectedly, one day she suddenly had a stomach ache and gave birth to that girl who was less than nine months old. Mrs. Someone often has a saying: 'Winning money is destined.' She believes that she does not have the fate of 'unexpected wealth,' and from this she knows that this time's winning money is the source of the child's birth, so she named her 'Tao Xi.' Because this is how she is pleasing!"

Although Tao Xi is six years old, she still can't speak properly, and can only count from one to three. But she has long recognized the characters of East, South, West, North, Center, Fa, One, Two, Three... Nine on the "Mahjong tiles." And strangely, when she sees the tiles, she changes. She is usually irritable and naughty, but when she goes with her mother to play Mahjong at the neighbor's house, she will sit at the corner of the table and stare blankly.

And she can help her mother take care of "missed tiles." If there are pairs in her mother's tiles, and someone plays out the same tile, she will shout "Pong" with her mother. Other than that, she is silent, her hands are drooping, her eyes are staring, just watching attentively. If sometimes her mother is missing three to complete a set, or three are missing one to complete a set, she will pay attention and call "Teacher Wang," "Mother Li" over, so her mother loves her the most, and even "Teacher Wang," "Mother Li" praises her as a "good child"!

When Mrs. Someone heard the words good child, she naturally added another layer of joy. She praised her daughter even more to others, and brought out the "Mahjong tiles" to test her in person. Then, most irrelevant people praised her again as a "smart child"!

The Four Northeast Company Commanders

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 26: Sadly Facing the Jade Mirror, I Grieve for My Beloved; Righteously Baring My Chest, I Forget My Family to Serve the Nation

Wangfujing Avenue, such a wide road, they were walking haphazardly, filling

an entire street. People on the street were all dodging and hiding. The more these short devils saw the Chinese like this, the more they swaggered with their arms and splayed legs, bumping into people on the street. The pitiful patrol police, always afraid of causing trouble on their turf, only dispersed the idle people on both sides of the street. Small stall owners and those carrying burdens ran everywhere. Because I was wearing gray clothes, they didn't dare shoo me away, only gave me a couple of glances. I also knew clearly that causing trouble would only make things difficult for the local authorities, so I had to step aside. But I clenched my fists, really wishing I could go up and beat two of them to death. After they had walked far away, I said, "Hmph! We'll meet on the front lines!" Company Commander, you didn't see the situation then, it really could make you spit out two mouthfuls of hot blood. That's why the words I said were only uttered after my lungs were bursting with anger. Guess what? Someone behind me sneered and said, "Just you?" When I turned around to look, the person had run away. The "you" he was referring to, I think, meant two things. First, he was saying that us soldiers didn't have the ability. Second, he heard my Northeastern accent and was saying that Northeasterners didn't have that kind of talent. But no matter which aspect he was talking about, I couldn't bear that kind of humiliation. Even now, when I think about it, I feel fire on the tips of my hair. If they ever organize a suicide squad on the front lines, count me, Wang, as one. As he spoke, he repeatedly patted his chest a few times. Zhao Ziqiang didn't say anything after hearing this, jumped into the pit, and tore off the red auspicious couplets pasted on the wall. Finally, even the little bits of red paper scraps that were left, he tore off as well. Wang Shili was a little bewildered by his sudden actions. Zhao Ziqiang tore the red paper completely clean before jumping down from the pit and smiling at Wang Shili: "You probably don't understand why I did this, right? I'll tell you, when I see this red paper, I think of happy events, and when I think of happy events, I naturally think of home. Always thinking like this can shatter a belly full of ambition, so I tore it off." (344)

Research on Inkstones (8)

— Wuliao Ke (Bored Guest)

General Overview of Duan Inkstones

Beautiful Patterns: Duan stone is considered to have beautiful patterns such as azure flowers, fish brain jelly, banana leaf white, sky blue, ice patterns, various fire marks, starling eyes, etc. Among the beautiful patterns, the azure flower is the most important. The names are very complex, and the forms are infinitely varied. The arguments about inkstones among the Japanese are only about azure flowers, and there is a reason for this.

A. Azure Flowers: "Stone Hidden Inkstone Talks" says that Song people generally didn't talk about azure flowers when discussing inkstones. Only "Ancient Inkstone Identification" began to use the phrase "drops are azure flowers" from Wu Shu's "Inkstone Ode" of the Tang Dynasty to prove the azure flower stone from the ancient pit. However, it only said that there were flower spots as big as chopsticks heads, like fine, clear jade.

It also says: "In the blackish-blue, there are white spots like millet, arranged like stars, a strange phenomenon, which does not match the modern discussion of azure flower iron. This is because the lower rock that was being mined at that time had not yet been dug to the depths." Later, as mining gradually

progressed, the essence was fully revealed, and the various forms of azure flowers were also recognized by many people. But everyone knows that azure flowers are precious, but no one has ever revealed why they are so precious. Even inkstone-loving writers only say: "Azure flowers are the essence of the stone;" "Only the finest stone has azure flowers." However, the reason for this extremely fine essence, they

cannot explain. The Japanese, on the other hand, have used scientific methods to study the reason for the special fineness of azure flowers from the essence of Duan stone. The book "Chinese Ancient Inkstones and Literature" by Bando Kanzan (translated by my colleague Hu Yizang) mentioned earlier has the following passage on azure flowers:

"What is the essence of azure flowers? In short, Duan stone belongs to

tuffaceous sedimentary rock. Its constituent molecules contain micro-molecules of diabase. These micro-molecules are scattered like fine dust, or aggregate to form coarse spots. Especially when these micro-molecules are distributed in stone with a hardness that is balanced with the inkstone surface, it is a supreme masterpiece (i.e., micro-dust azure flowers). However, it is very difficult to obtain such fine products, because the crystal shape of the stone is mostly uneven. The reason why Duan stone has fewer of these is due to the power of these diabase micro-molecules. Ink produced on inkstones with these micro-molecules has a luster that is completely different from the ordinary."

And in its discussion of stone eyes, it says:

"The substance of stone eyes is stone-linked worms, and its main body is mixed with diabase. The stone-linked worms are shaped like maggots or earthworms. The body of this worm is calcareous. The calcareous substance is washed away, and diabase seeps into it, solidifying it. The Duan people say that stone with azure veins must have eyes, which is the manifestation of diabase."

The Japanese are accustomed to studying mineralogy, so they have this discovery. In the past, China did not have this scientific knowledge.

We only know that azure means azure flowers, but in fact, it is not entirely azure. The dense micro-dust azure flowers are almost black, while the light ant-foot azure flowers are almost light white, light green, or pale red, and pale yellow. Therefore, when discussing azure flowers, one must not be stuck to one shape or one color, but understand them spiritually to know their wonder. "Stone Flower's" discussion of azure flowers says, "Azure flowers should be fine, not coarse; lively, not dull; deep, not exposed; blurred, not clustered; and whole, not broken." Micro-dust is the most precious, followed by goose down, then ant feet (also known as fly feet), then goose down clusters (i.e., azure flower clusters), then rose purple, and then fly heads (i.e., parent-child azure flowers). Other forms that are patchy, lined up, coarse, and dry are not worth valuing. And "Stone Hidden's" discussion also includes names such as fly wings, duckweed, fish schools, and taro patterns. There is also the so-called winter melon pulp, which Gao Guqi considered a masterpiece. In addition, there are rain-soaked wall azure flowers and clam belly pattern azure flowers mentioned in previous writings. However, the Japanese consider rain-soaked wall azure flowers to be as precious as micro-dust, saying that late Qing literati admired this product. If they encountered this stone, they would hide it under a stone slab, unwilling to carve it. Winter melon pulp, on the other hand, is only regarded as a medium product, like taro patterns shaped like stone flower vegetables. Furthermore, Mr. Bando said that when "Stone Flower" wrote the history of inkstones, he only

listed rose purple azure flowers as second-class. Later, in his reply to his friend Wang Hezhou, he called rose purple a famous material unique to Water Return Cave, which should be listed above all azure flowers. From this, it can be seen that the preferences for inkstones, and the criticism of good or bad, also differ even within a short period of time.

Securities and Public Bonds Slightly Suppressed, Then Rise

The First Session Once Fell

The Second Session's Rising Trend Resumes

The 22 Customs Rose by More Than One Yuan, the Most Significant

Yesterday, at the Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange, the short retracement that occurred at the opening session, although in line with predictions, was very temporary. The rising trend resumed and was even more intense than before. Slightly suppressed, they then rose, their flames were flourishing. Although short selling was significant, long-term covering and new longs were also quite active. The high morale of the market was unprecedented. When market prices were slightly pressured, their reaction was particularly strong. When short sellers briefly reduced pressure, their reaction created a new high price. The rise in market prices was actually gradually pushed forward by shorts. Observing the environment, high public bonds and low prices formed an inverse proportion. The more difficult it was for commodities to circulate, the more restricted the use of cash became. Therefore, the abnormal development of public bonds was still in its early stages. Even if there were retracements, they would be limited. However, one should not forget the danger in heights, and it is also necessary to be cautious. Currently, the Salt Tax market price has reached above 65%, and the squeeze is particularly severe due to the approaching delivery. After this, it may stabilize slightly, but it is feared that there may not be a significant drop. The events of yesterday showed that the opening situation was quite unstable. It started flat, and after entering, No. 38 was sold frantically, causing a decline, retracing by half a yuan. However, the shorts took the opportunity to cover, and the rebound in the second session was even more intense. Salt Tax rose by six or seven jiao, and 22 Customs spot goods were not yet on the market. The shorts' panic was especially self-inflicted. The squeeze was particularly severe, and the price soared by 1.34 yuan in one session. The pain of floating shorts was such. In the afternoon's two sessions, the rising momentum did not subside, and the closing was slightly weaker compared to the morning. However, the rising trend of Salt Tax was still strong, and 96 suddenly rose by eight or nine jiao, showing the longs' strong intentions. There were many old examples of this kind of behavior. It was nothing more than that the market prices of the various bonds had become high, and many had become boring, so the targets were changed. There was no reason for it. New York Stock Market Shows Slight Progress

According to a report from Sin Fung Foreign Firm based on the Wall Street Journal, the New York Stock Exchange market was still sluggish yesterday. However, due to the exceptionally good business report of U.S. Steel, silver speculators continued their activities, and there were unconfirmed rumors of a gold price increase, the market showed slight progress. Large speculators and the public mostly remained on the sidelines, awaiting the outcome of labor disputes and the development of the exchange management case. The small exchange market advanced with gold mining stocks. There was considerable selling of U.S. government bonds, influenced by the gold price rumors, and at the same time, bondholders were deeply worried that the silver bill would become law, causing considerable anxiety. Speculative bonds recovered to high levels, while foreign bonds were soft. Furthermore, according to agent reports, there was good demand for (securities) because the strike is about to be postponed, and the exchange management case shows signs of further modification. (Wheat) Business showed slight progress; the southwest and northwest are becoming increasingly arid, and news from Washington is more favorable than before—do not short sell. (Cotton) The market entered a standstill, awaiting developments from all sides. There was foreign selling, and factories bought when prices fell. Labor unrest is expanding, and some say that southern yarn factories will also strike, while opinions are increasingly divided between those who favor cooperation and those who favor compulsory reduction of cotton fields. The yarn and cloth market is sluggish, but buyers' needs are gradually increasing. Recently, due to many parties divesting, the market position has already improved, but a surge in market prices still awaits changes in the current situation. Total daily trading volume was 1,020,000 shares. The Dow Jones New York indices are listed below:

Yarn, Cotton, and Futures Yarn Are All in a Slump

丨Bulls Heavily Trapped丨

The yarn market was flat in the morning and fell in the afternoon, with the situation remaining weak and showing no signs of recovery. Given the unfavorable surrounding environment, sluggishness is necessary. As the delivery period approaches, goods entering warehouses are very enthusiastic, thus increasing the pressure on the yarn market. Combined with foreign merchants causing trouble from behind, it is difficult for factory solidarity to be consistent, making it even harder to consolidate the market. However, the bottom has dried up, and factories are losing money, so there will not be an excessive drop.

Futures Yarn First Rises Then Falls The opening price of standard yarn in the morning market, after a big fall, triggered profit-takers to cover their positions. The market atmosphere slightly stabilized, and each month rose by 1.2.4 jiao. In the afternoon, news came that spot yarn sales were quiet, and each month fell by 1.2.4.6 jiao to 1 yuan and 1 jiao. Overseas Cotton Markets Fall Across the Board

Yesterday, the US cotton market initially fell due to unfavorable news from Liverpool, then rebounded strongly due to Wall Street's strength. Later, it weakened again due to foreign selling. Excessive Long Positions Cause Flour Prices to Fall

Yesterday, the flour market saw a downward trend across near and far months after the opening in the morning. Due to the continuous rise in market prices in recent days, prices were up by 7-8 fen to nearly a jiao compared to the low prices at the beginning of the month. However, this did not lead to any real offtake, but rather created an opportunity for general hoarding and buying. Therefore, after the opening price in the morning, various hoarding and hedging long positions took the opportunity to sell off. Although factories did not sell off, they also lacked purchases. However, speculators still had strong interest, and in addition to the return of long positions, there was also short covering. Total daily trading volume was 320,000 bags, which was still considered lively in the recent sluggish trading period. However, with more selling than buying, buying interest became even more sluggish in the afternoon. Therefore, forward contracts saw more short selling. The closing price was down 2 fen for this month, down 2.75 fen for next month, down 2.5 fen for May, down 1.5 fen for June and July, and down 1.75 fen for August.

Wheat Market Futures Weak, Spot Firm

Yesterday, the wheat market saw very little activity in imported wheat. After the opening price of standard wheat, there were long positions selling off in the near term, and the declining flour market caused sentiment to trend downward. March and April saw a consistent decline, while there were still new buyers inquiring about the forward contracts. The final closing price was down 5 fen for March, down 4 fen for April, up 1 fen for July, and up 2 fen for August. Spot wheat saw active arrivals and sales, and the market was also slightly firm. Shandong wheat was priced at 3 yuan and 6 jiao and 2 fen, Yaowan at 3 yuan and 6 jiao, Bengbu at 3 yuan and 5 jiao and 2 fen, Linhua at 3 yuan and 5 jiao and 4 fen, and Mingguang Yingzhou at 3 yuan and 5 jiao and 7 fen, totaling 3,000 bags, which were purchased by Fuxin.

Sutong and Nan Gang Rice Fell Another 5 Fen

North Market Common Japonica Rice Not Available Due to Disputes

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, there were more than 40 sources, totaling over 6,000 shi, with late rice accounting for the majority and thick japonica rice accounting for a small portion. Sales were slow, and the market did not look promising at the beginning. Few customers came to the street, with only a slight movement from customers from other provinces. Sellers found it difficult to manage this situation, and if they wanted to tighten prices, they worried about leftover goods, so they had to call for flat prices. The northern and southern ocean firms then began to purchase goods. Firms from Xiamen and other places paid attention to Fengjing, Xilian, Nangang, and Zhongguan late rice. Weihaiwei and Tianjin firms favored Qingjiao and Songjiang high-quality goods, totaling more than 2,000 bags. Regarding the distribution problem, it was heard that both the customer firms and their landlords were restricted by the price limits in the telegrams, so the market depreciated by 4-5 fen. The thick japonica rice in the stores of the various firms was sluggish, and the market outlook was weak, so the market color was not bleak. The prices of Sutong and Nangang goods fell by 5 fen. Only the common japonica rice in the common firm stood firm at the original price due to a shortage of goods. The delivery of Du Yangjian Lai was integrated into sales, without any change in price. Although the route for Yin Bian Yuan was not broad, the market color tightened again due to the scarcity of goods, but there was not much difference in price.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, there were more than 20 sources from He Xia. The offtake of various goods in the market was still slow. The market shape of white japonica rice, thin rice, customer indica rice, Yin Yuan, and White Yuan was flat and weak. The firm stopped trading due to disputes.

Additional Ten Batches of South-North Goods and Orchid Seeds Arrive

丨New Mutton from Shikou Arrives in Three Boxes Yesterday丨

After the previous batch of orchid seeds arrived and opened at 48 yuan, the market was very strong due to early depletion of inventory. Yesterday, it was heard that Taikoo Company's Linan ship arrived with a batch, with only 20 remaining. Samples were immediately shown, and buyers rushed to purchase due to the good color and eggs, making it difficult to bargain.

New Shikou mutton had been in short supply for a long time, and recent sales had been active. Yesterday, the Linan ship arrived with three boxes. The samples showed a bright color and large size, making them top-notch. They were immediately sold for 97 yuan. If not much more arrives, the market looks stable.

The Listed Prices of Both British and American Tinplate Have Increased

The listed prices of both British and American tinplate were reported to have increased yesterday. British and American 90-pound boxes were sold for 16 shillings and 2 pence per box, up 2 pence from before, and 100-pound boxes were sold for 17 shillings and 2 pence, also up 3 pence. American 90-pound boxes were sold for 4 gold yuan and 3 jiao and 7 fen, and 200-pound boxes were sold for 5 yuan and 9 jiao, up 2 jiao. Due to oversupply in the Shanghai market, industry peers adopted a hands-off approach to order business, so no purchases were heard.

Spot Hunan pure antimony, which is trending higher due to scarcity, was reportedly shipped from Hankou yesterday in more than ten tons, so the market outlook is expected to be lively again.

Free Talk

After Reading "Literature's" "Translation Special Issue"

— Yu Yangling

An ancient person said, "Other people's wives are better, one's own articles are better." Looking at the state of the reading world in recent years, we can say this: "Foreign writers are better, but domestic articles are better."

Gorky, Shaw, Romain Rolland, Barbusse, Gide, Sinclair... these names, and the deeds related to these names, are often talked about, and readers, when they read these names, are also invariably respectful, complimenting them as "literary giants." As for domestic writers, many are "unprincipled," and those who are principled are definitely not as great as foreign writers, which is also a recognized fact. However, even though foreign literary giants are great, no one wants to read their works. Conversely, even though domestic writers are "unprincipled," their articles can still be popular.

The relationship between writers and articles, among Chinese readers, has become so disparate that it is truly strange. But this history has been long. Many years ago, Xu Zhimo, such a "poet philosopher," already admired "Call to Arms" while completely denying the personality of the author of "Call to Arms." As for the translated versions of the works of Tolstoy, Dostoevsky, Gorky, and other writers whose great names have been heard for a long time, they have remained scarce for the past twenty years.

The reason, most people say, lies in the poor quality of the translations. "Literal translation" and "hard translation" are incomprehensible, and "smooth translation" is not very trustworthy. The translation world has not yet invented a proper translation method: so people simply don't read them. As for the works of domestic writers, whether good or bad, they first of all get a straightforward reception, so there are always more people who love to read them, especially now when people treat reading articles as pure leisure.

Whether creative writing or translation, it is nothing more than a commodity today. Since translations have no customers, many translators have also put down their pens. In the corners of several magazines, one or two translations are occasionally embellished, just like hanging a homespun underpants next to fine silk in a brothel, it is just "unable to avoid vulgarity, just so."

However, this time, the "Literature" magazine has specially published a translation special issue, and aims to "slightly show a glimpse of the current state of world literature, and hope to use this to arouse discussion on various translation issues." It has a great intention to save the situation from collapse. This is a very noteworthy thing in the literary world in recent years. The relationship between world literature and China, and the future of the Chinese translation world, will depend on the outcome of this move.

I have already finished reading this special issue, which contains writers from twelve countries, various genres, a total of twenty pieces of writing. These twenty articles are not all top choices in world literature, but they are not necessarily worse than China's first-class works. As for the translation style, they can all make people feel effortless and reassured when reading. I originally wanted to make a critique of each article, but unfortunately, I don't understand the popular critical formula of "...very good, but...makes people dissatisfied, but...still...besides...a little...as for...is very noteworthy."

I can only say in general, these twenty articles will not necessarily make you feel flawless, but they will definitely not make you gain nothing. And what is particularly noteworthy is the many opinions on translation in the "Forum."

Following this special issue, "Literature" will also publish a "Creative Writing Special Issue." If you read this special issue first, and then read the next issue, then you will have a deeper understanding of the issues of world literature and translation.

Bathe in the Yi River, Enjoy the Breeze at the Rain Altar

— Bai Ge

Now, there are already people advocating governing the world with half of the "Analects"! In the past, I believed this. Because at that time, the ways of managing the family, governing the country, and bringing peace to the world that the teacher taught me never went beyond the "Four Books," and the "Great Learning," "Doctrine of the Mean," and "Mencius" were really just Zengzi, Zisi, and Mencius inheriting Confucius's intentions. Naturally, the "Analects," which records Confucius's own holy words and deeds, would be the representative. In fact, I myself didn't particularly like using those words and deeds as standards to rectify my heart and cultivate myself to reach that initial step. However, I still remember a few words that really captivated me, and that is:

"In late spring, when the spring clothes are ready, with five or six adults and six or seven children, bathing in the Yi River, enjoying the breeze at the Rain Altar, and returning while singing."

Whenever I read this passage, I felt that the Confucius in the teacher's mouth was really unreliable. Confucius was not a solemn and unapproachable person. At least he wasn't as rigid as my teacher, who specifically forbade students from swimming in the river and singing along the way. Therefore, I also resented my rigid teacher very much. At the same time, a kind of hope grew in my heart day by day along with that resentment: I only hoped for an opportunity to bathe in the Yi River and enjoy the breeze at the Rain Altar, so that I could personally experience that feeling.

Two years ago, I finally got this opportunity. On the third day after I arrived in Qufu, taking advantage of the leisure time before the school started, I went to the Rain Altar with several colleagues to "observe the wind." At that time, it was still the cold first month of the year, and no one really wanted to enjoy the breeze, so we only said we were going to observe. It is said that the Rain Altar was the place where earth dances were held during the time of the State of Lu. People living in Qufu probably love to say that any so-called historical site or scenic spot came from the State of Lu or that Confucius once did this or that here. I don't necessarily believe this "it is said," and naturally it is not easy to develop extra interest because of it. This altar, in name, is said to be an altar, but in reality, it is a small hill, so small that it is as big as a grave mound. On top of it stands a stele, like a vertical, lidless box, or like a vertical, lidless coffin. The words on the stele are no longer very clear. Next to it is an old but short tree of some kind, and the rest of the place is completely bald, with hardly any small trees to be found. The surroundings are full of wheat fields, and to take a shortcut, you still have to walk through the green wheat fields. If it weren't for its fame, I think even people passing by would only sit on the ridges of the wheat fields to take a breath and would not go up there again. Thus, the saying "came with enthusiasm, left with disappointment" became a true depiction of our day.

Later, when the summer vacation was approaching, it was still driven by a kind of curiosity that I invited several colleagues to swim in the Yi River. Leaving the city along the South Gate, a vast expanse of farmland and a small stream planted with trees on both sides first made people fascinated, thinking that the Yi River must be waiting for us "clear and rippling," and that we would soon be able to merge into its embrace. After walking for a long time and taking many twists and turns, we finally arrived at the Yi River that we had longed for, but we didn't know that it would be so disappointing. The shallow riverbed, the still river water, neither wide nor deep, was simply impossible to bathe in. But other colleagues had already jumped into the water first, and a childhood game reappeared before my eyes, so I had to quickly undress and jump down. The water was warm, and the greatest advantage was that it did not become turbid even after prolonged disturbance. It turned out that there was fine sand without soil underneath, so it seemed very turbid, but in fact it was very clear. Everyone used that fine sand to rub their bodies, and I did the same, feeling that it was a little smoother than ordinary sand. After getting ashore, they still used the dry sand on the shore to wash their feet, and they even used that dry sand to dry their feet and put on their shoes and socks directly! This made me a little surprised. At that time, I realized that this was the way to bathe here. So I was extremely happy and immediately ran to the Rain Altar with great enthusiasm.

This time, returning to the Rain Altar was no longer as disappointing as before. The cool breeze softly brushed against my face, immediately making me feel the warmth of the two sentences, "The southern breeze is gentle, it can relieve the people's worries." At that time, it can truly be said that I was happy and forgot my worries, and fully experienced the true meaning of "bathing in the Yi River, enjoying the breeze at the Rain Altar."

Two-Headed Boat

— Fu

—— Folk Song of Eastern Zhejiang

(I)

Long eyelashes, black eyes,

Cause trouble and arouse pity;

Straddling one foot on a two-headed boat,

Which head is heavier and which is lighter?

(II)

White shell teeth, red cherry lips,

Seemingly heartless yet affectionate;

Straddling one foot on a two-headed boat,

Which head floats and which head sinks?

"Old Wine Can't Be Put in New Bottles"

— Meng Ke

In China, not to mention periodicals and magazines, even for daily newspapers, those that sell over ten thousand copies probably number only two or three. This clearly demonstrates that the number of citizens who can read and afford newspapers is just this many. This can be considered a unique characteristic of China, or to put it bluntly, it's actually quite a sad situation.

In previous years, there were indeed people advocating for a "literacy movement." Now, it seems everyone avoids even mentioning it. I believe the reason is that most of those educators from the "May Fourth Movement" who considered themselves progressive are now very busy. Some are running around with national affairs, some are attending international academic conferences, and some are even retreating into the mountains and forests, composing poems, drinking wine, telling jokes, and writing letters, leaving them with no time to attend to "this."

However, the illiterate, or rather, those who have no way to become literate among the Chinese population, are still unintentionally receiving a kind of education. In major cities, on the cement sidewalks of roads, and at the iron gates of alleys, one can often see men and children who look very unkempt, crowding around to look at "comic strip pictures." They are satisfying their thirst for knowledge through the intuitive art form. As a result, their minds are filled with emperors and deities. Superstition and the mentality of servitude still tightly bind their hearts.

Recently, however, due to discussions in several magazines about a certain literary issue, one or two writers who genuinely care about mass education have been drawn from written language to the "comic strip pictures" in art, wanting to advocate for a movement to improve "comic strip pictures." This is truly gratifying. However, some have raised objections, believing that "old wine cannot be put in new bottles" and that a new artistic educational tool should be "created." Recently, some daily newspapers in Shanghai have indeed been trying to create new forms of "comic strip pictures." However, the effects of these attempts are quite interesting, either resulting in "the intellectual class considering it not art, while the masses still cannot understand it," or ending up with neither the masses nor the intellectual class being able to understand it. Naturally, we cannot draw conclusions on the issue based on this single experience, but from this alone, we can learn a lesson: that before the old society is thoroughly reformed, trying to immediately change a trend or habit is extremely difficult. We can only utilize it as much as possible and gradually transform it. Therefore, based on the lessons of reality, I believe that we should still accept the old form of "comic strip pictures" conditionally and incorporate new ideas into it as much as possible.

From this, it can be seen that in literature, conditionally utilizing the old form of chapter novels, which are more popular among the petty bourgeoisie, is also a similarly important issue.

In short, regarding this type of issue, all those who are still genuinely concerned about mass education really need to bring it up again for discussion.

A Tentative Translation of the Book of Odes

— Yu Shixia

The Cypress Boat

I.

Piloting a cypress boat,

Letting it drift with the flow.

My heart is restless and sleepless,

As if with deep sorrow.

Could it be I have no wine?

I'll force a drunken outing!

II.

My heart is not a bright mirror,

Cannot take it to reflect.

Though I have brothers,

Cannot rely on them.

Should I try to pour out my pain,

They will grow furious.

Miscellaneous Notes from a Journey West (5)

— Lu Yan

After the train passes Zhengzhou, it is no longer a sandy plain. The low-lying areas and ravines on both sides gradually increase, but although they are ravines, there is no water. Now, they are all roads for people or vehicles to travel. Our train travels among the low hills from time to time. There are many trees on both sides. Tall and straight poplars stand in a continuous row. Afterward, the hills gradually become higher, the ravines become lower, and the train also travels slower. Holes one after another up, down, left, and right, these are the old houses people live in today. They live in such places, wearing ragged clothes, eating black bread, and the fruits of their labor must still be supplied to the officials for cement, silk, Western food, cars, and all luxuries.

The road becomes more and more difficult to travel. The train often tilts, and ravines dozens of feet deep appear from time to time beside the tracks. The driver drives as if approaching a deep abyss, driving particularly slowly, cautiously and gently. After dragging more than half of the train carriages, he suddenly drives quickly, fearing that the rear carriages will fall into the pit, as if wanting to drag them over regardless of life or death. The hills on both sides whistle and roar, helping him. The train also whistles from time to time, rumbling into the dark mountain tunnels, passing through one after another, a total of eleven to Luoyang.

On the train, I saw the White Horse Temple from afar, and also saw the ruins of a mausoleum. When I asked someone, they said it was Emperor Xian of Han's. As the train entered the Luoyang boundary, I saw tall tombstones all the way, presumably the family tombs of officials of all sizes in the past. In the fields, the raised mounds of earth, the size of water vats, foot basins, and face basins, are the graves of the common people. In a few years, these water vat-sized mounds will become foot basin-sized; foot basin-sized mounds will become face basin-sized; and face basin-sized mounds will be plowed into flat ground, and things will be planted on them, and they will no longer be recognizable. For the sake of land production, this is correct. If every dead person were buried like the customs of my hometown or like the way the nobles here do it, then after many years, the cultivable land would gradually become narrower, and the world would become a true graveyard. Life is a grain of sand. Where is it forever?

A traveler who got off the train in Luoyang told me that the flies in Luoyang bite people, and when you kill them, you actually find blood coming out. I said, I'm afraid it's something like horseflies? But he said no, it's ordinary flies. I felt strange.

West of Luoyang, I often see a kind of pine and cypress tree, its leaves growing all the way down to the base of the trunk. It is said that when Zhao Kuangyin went to Tongguan, he was afraid that he would not recognize the way back, so he tied grass to the lower end of the tree trunks all the way, and therefore later it became like this kind of tree.

From Luoyang to Tongguan, we passed through fourteen or fifteen more mountain tunnels, with the Xiashi Post Station being the longest. After passing Baozi, we could see the Yellow River at any time. The steep and secluded danger, this kind of place, has now been passed. Although the train travels on newly opened flat roads, it is still dangerous enough. The only thing that disappointed me was that the mountains were all barren soil, and it was almost impossible to see even a small stone. The color was neither red-yellow nor black, but a lifeless color close to yellow but not yellow, close to white but not white. And it is so loose that it can collapse at any time, just like human life.

Folk Song

— Fu Changyu

Airplanes fly in the sky,

Cannons pass on the ground;

Trains carry soldiers,

Handcarts carry fodder.

The rich go to the Western-style streets,

The poor dig cellars.

Last Testament (4)

— Lin Huiyin

Yina is in Xi Zhuoyun's office.

"Very good; you've written it well, thank you."

"I wonder which issue it will be published in?"

"Today is Monday. It's too late for Wednesday, the manuscripts have already been submitted. It's also too late for Saturday. I think next Wednesday I've already discussed it with He Jiemu, and asked him to make a small ending to his novel so that yours can be published. Let me tell him again; I think next Wednesday will be possible, at most one more issue apart, until next Saturday."

"Can I get all the publication fees within the year?" After hesitating for a second or two, she finally asked.

"You're also waiting for money?" Smiling, as if not believing it.

She nodded with a smile.

"As long as it can be published in one or two issues within the year, and it can be published within the year," Zhuoyun said without hesitation.

"I also want to sell the copyright fee, is that okay?"

"Yes, you can."

"Can I get the money at the time?"

"It's probably not a problem Wang Zhonghua also wanted money for the Mid-Autumn Festival, so he sold the copyright of his "Cold Night." Thirteen said, and he got the money on the fourteenth."

"Then, thank you, please go and talk about it."

"But, it's best to have someone write a letter to me, writing about wanting to sell the copyright; with this letter, it's more convenient to talk about it."

Yina promised to send him the written letter in a day or two.

Two or three days after sending the letter, Yina called Xi Zhuoyun, asking him what the publishing department's reply was. Zhuoyun said that the reply had not yet come, but that "Taste of Life" had been decided to be published starting next Saturday. She knew that next Saturday was the 20th, and that from that issue, there would be three more issues that could be published within the year. As long as she could get the publication fees, even if the copyright couldn't be sold for a while, it wouldn't matter much, so she wasn't too uneasy in her heart.

That fateful Saturday arrived. As soon as Yina woke up, she asked Li Ma to bring her the newspaper for the day. She hurriedly looked for new book advertisements. She found the Literary Semimonthly, but in the table of contents, there was no "Taste of Life." The name of its author, Chen Yina, did not show the slightest trace.

Her heart was beating fast.

Shenbao Local Supplement

Commentary

Shanghai's Silver Reserves Total 560 Million

— Mingtang

Recently, the Economic Research Office of the Bank of China announced that Shanghai's silver reserves total 560 million yuan, of which more than 280 million yuan are deposited in Chinese merchant banks, and more than 270 million yuan are deposited in foreign banks. It is estimated that China's total silver reserves are only more than one billion yuan (previously seen in a certain statistic, it seems to be 1.2 or 1.3 billion yuan, I don't know if there are any errors, but it is probably this number), and Shanghai alone accounts for more than 40% of the total; and among this more than 40%, foreign banks account for slightly less than one-half. This is truly an alarming ratio.

Why has China's economy developed this kind of deformed form? Undoubtedly, it is because of the bankruptcy of the rural areas in the interior, and the concentration of cash in the cities, resulting in such an obese phenomenon. This is common sense that most people know.

Then, what is the only use of such a huge amount of silver reserves in Shanghai? Here, let's look at the business conditions of various banks in Shanghai. According to the Shenbao Yearbook; the general business conditions of 28 banks, including the Central Bank, members of the Shanghai Banking Association in the 20th year of the Republic of China, the total assets of various banks were 2.5 billion 36,000 yuan, of which negotiable securities accounted for 234.767 million yuan. Although this amount is not very large compared to the total assets, it is still alarming when viewed in terms of the ratio of various asset departments. In addition, there are huge investments in real estate. As for the amount of loans, although there are more than 1.5 billion, in which department is most of this 1.5 billion loan invested? Because we have not seen the business classification table of the above banks, we cannot determine it. But it is probably not mostly invested in the production sector, this is certain. This only needs to look at the crisis of our country's national industry in recent years, and we can know that prudent bankers will never be willing to invest useful money in dangerous areas, then most of the assets can only be used for speculative undertakings. From this point, we can also see that in China's economy in recent years, not only is the countryside bankrupt, but also the productive enterprises in the cities have reached a state of decline.

50% of Shanghai's silver reserves are deposited in foreign banks, which shows that China's economy as a whole is a colonial economy; and the degree of this colonial economy is only deepening year by year. The economic lifeline of the whole country is almost entirely controlled by foreign banks. The so-called Chinese merchant banks are just looking up to them.

Not only do Chinese merchant banks have to rely on foreign banks, but foreign banks also directly control China's entire politics. Politics depends on the economy, this is certain. Whoever has money can manipulate whomever. Foreign banks hold such economic hegemony in China, how can they not go on to influence politics? There are many examples, and there is no need to list them all here.

Why do foreign banks hold such huge silver reserves in China? Undoubtedly, they all come from our people. In addition to indirectly taking it from the Chinese countryside, there are also a large number of feudal classes and comprador classes in China, who deposit a large amount of people's wealth that they have plundered into foreign banks for the sake of "safety." In this way, foreign banks become even more affluent.

The countryside is extremely bankrupt, the national industry has reached the final crisis, all the cash in China is concentrated in the cities, and half of it flows into foreign banks (an even larger amount flows overseas). Chinese merchant banks invest most of this urban floating capital in securities, real estate and other speculative undertakings. What will the result be?

I Am So Young

— Wang Ci

I am so young!

According to my age, I am not qualified to be a primary school teacher who makes a living by using my voice; but, who would have thought that I

have been one for two full years already.

The powder of chalk is about to bury my youth!

Once, a child in the sixth grade, who was much taller than me, sincerely asked me in the classroom:

"Is Teacher Wang a middle school graduate?"

"Yes."

"How old is Teacher Wang? You look so young!" His facial expression told me how much he envied me!

My eyelashes could no longer hold back my tears I suddenly cried.

All the children in the classroom were surprised and were softly inquiring about the reason why I was crying who would know.

One of the children stood up and questioned the child who had asked me the question earlier:

"What did you say to offend Teacher Wang?"

Quiet quiet...

The sound of footsteps moved to my front, and stammering words were sent to my ears:

"Teacher Wang; what did I say to offend Teacher Wang, you can punish me you can punish me..."

Unexpectedly, he also started to cry.

I pushed him away and said to them with a sob:

"There's nothing I just thought I was so young, and I started crying."

From then on, the children never dared to mention the word "young" in front of me again.

I am so young!

The powder of chalk is about to bury my youth!

Another time, I was looking at a few little babies in the kindergarten on the playground jumping rope actively, doing two and then counting:

"Two! Four! Six! Eight! Ten!..."

How interesting!

I walked over:

"Good babies! I'll come too, okay?"

The little babies looked at me, smiled, shook their heads, and said:

"No, no! We can't beat you, you're the teacher!"

Unexpectedly, they dragged the rope and ran away.

I turned around, and the sentence "You are the teacher" got into my heart; returning to my bedroom, I lay down on the pillow and cried again.

I can't squeeze into the children's team anymore.

But, I am so young!

The powder of chalk is about to bury my youth!

A Lesson in Dealing with the World

— Jianshe

Commerce, I have no way to name it. To put it bluntly, it is that even rotten goods are advertised as good goods for sale, and even sow meat is advertised as good pork. This is what is called commerce.

Originally, many things are always like this. Unless you actually delve into the core of those things, you will never know whether these things are good or bad. The reason for this is that many things have their own different and exceptionally beautiful exteriors. Usually, people without sharp eyes are always unable to see whether these things are good or bad.

Therefore, so-called intermediaries are needed here. In the field of literature and art, so-called critics are needed. Obviously, the task of these intermediaries and critics is to use their sharp eyes to tell us the actual situation. For example, this cup of tea is bitter and really cannot be drunk. In this way, we will naturally avoid it.

However, this will annoy people. And if this kind of thing continues to develop, it will definitely eliminate commerce.

Annoying people and eliminating commerce are both bad. To be a person, one must be a person who pleases everyone. The tea is bitter, let others drink it; it is clearly sow meat, let others buy it. At most, you will feel somewhat uncomfortable in your heart, but in reality, you must not provoke real enemies. If you are smart, you will not only not expose the truth about this bitter tea, but instead, you will promote everywhere that the tea leaves in a certain place are good, and that it is not worth living a lifetime if you do not buy some to drink. In this way, you will not only have tea to drink without spending a penny, but the tea merchant will also give you some extra money.

If this is the case, then you are of course the most adept at dealing with the world. On the one hand, commerce can be developed, and on the other hand, you can also become rich.

There are probably many such people among the four hundred million compatriots. However, although some people act quite like and are used to it, they are still a bit vague about the theory, so I specially take some time to write it down, hoping that people with intentions will choose to adopt it.

A Sketch of Mood

— Liu An

Last year, Peng Jiahuang died of illness. When the literary and art circles held a memorial service for him, I thought to myself that a person who struggled bitterly with life finally died in defeat, and that the road of life is really difficult to walk; later, Zhu Xiang committed suicide by drowning himself. When the magazine published a special issue for him, I thought to myself that a person who could not fight against the oppression of life even committed suicide. On the one hand, it showed bravery, and on the other hand, it showed weakness. In the end, life should be lived bravely. The deaths of these two people did not stir up the waves in my heart. This year, Ai Xia committed suicide by taking medicine, and the newspapers mourned her endlessly. I just said that people are too serious about life, and there is only one way for him to go, which is suicide. Recently, I suddenly had the idea of praising suicide, but the motive was inexplicable even to myself. In the deep of night, thinking deeply in bed, analyzing myself, I felt that my mood had really changed.

Could it be that I am becoming pessimistic because of the suffering of politics? But this kind of pessimistic mood did not just arise now. To put it closer, it was last year, and to put it further, it was three years ago. Last year, I announced that I would not ask about politics, which was a public matter. Three years ago, I published a collection of novels, all of which were nihilistic works, but people didn't pay attention to it. The pessimism of my heart is not enough to prove the origin of the idea of praising suicide, this is obvious.

The old fisherman repeatedly begged for mercy from the thugs, but he had already been beaten until his head was bleeding. The two young fishermen saw that he was pitiful, so they carried him back from the gate of the Ding family. They just sighed coldly all the way; they never thought about how to resist oppression!

Fishing and Killing the Family

— Meng

Xiao En and his daughter fished until late, then returned home along the way; the neighboring fishermen told them that the old fisherman had been beaten for owing fish tax! His leg was badly injured; his ear was bleeding a lot. Xiao En sighed after hearing this: "It's too hard to be poor!"

However, I also have the idea of praising suicide, but I don't want to commit suicide. Instead, I yearn to live on, no matter what, I have to live on. I feel trembling about death. This is a contradiction, and it is even more terrible than wanting to commit suicide. Thinking carefully in the quiet night, and analyzing it, it is because I already have the heart of an old man. According to age, I am in my prime, but now I already have the heart of an old man. What hope do I want to say about life?

Old people don't want to die, so there are no old people who commit suicide; but old people are not serious about life, and live casually. This is what is frightening. My mood is now changing like this, probably a sign that everything is over, alas!

The Old Fisherman

Xiao En Xiao Guiying Fisherman

Wishing to Be Reincarnated as a Man in the Next Life

— Qi Ping

It is difficult to be a person, and it is even more difficult to be a woman. Although some people think that women always take advantage everywhere, in fact, this is just superficial talk. Looking at our old star, Ms. Wang Hanlun, being fed foot dirt and nasal mucus by her husband, we can know how difficult it is to be a woman.

Apple face, cherry lips, what does it matter to you? Eyes like autumn waves, waist like willow branches, all of these are born of heaven, how can I be a demon! Why bother the poets and writers, who use their writing skills to spread paper and soak ink, to criticize and scold women, whether horizontally or vertically, and to make a lot of four-six essays on snow, moon, wind, and flowers. The modern brothers then fill the pages with sisters! Darling! and embellish some sensual poems, making people's flesh shudder, so it seems that without women, one cannot write articles, but to write articles, one cannot do without women. Let's not mention this for the time being, but some are even more absurd and unexpected, even pushing the matter of China's extermination onto women. What about King Zhou being destroyed by Daji, King You being destroyed by Bao Si, and Dong Zhuo undoubtedly being killed by Diao Chan, and the recent loss of the three northeastern provinces, also seems to be because of a certain lady's winking eyes, which made our young general happy and confused about how he lost such a large area of 30 million square miles! Ah! So indiscriminately, openly insulting my female compatriots, it really makes me, a crowd of women, want to jump into the Huangpu River to clear myself!

In the offices and on the roads, from the well-dressed gentlemen in suits and leather shoes to the rough-footed peddlers, what makes people spit and savor is nothing more than women. Whose girl's eyebrows are thick, whose girl's thighs are white, it seems that there is nothing to say other than this. Originally, women in the eyes of men are just playthings. When they like you, they will be so diligent to call you elder sister that you can hardly believe it. When they are tired of playing with you, then it is not to mention that they will turn their heads and leave, strangers on the road, it is all the same. And the virginity of young girls is destroyed in this unconsciousness. How dangerous! How difficult it is to be a woman!

Women, women have their own indelible achievements. What kind of Confucius is he, daring to make such a bold statement as: "Only women and villains are difficult to raise." The words are so absurd, not only insulting his mother, but simply insulting my sisters all over the world. Probably the old gentleman must have been frustrated in love, or at least received the cold shoulder from women, so a burst of resentment, unable to suppress it, so he bit words and came up with such slanderous words, as a means of revenge.

Before! Women could only be confined to their boudoirs, not allowed to take a step outside the door. A good pair of natural feet had to be tied as tightly as bamboo slips, in order to convey a smile to the philanderers. Now, although it is said that they are liberated, they can also work in society, but what else is there besides getting the beautiful name of a vase? Ah! Unfortunate to be born a woman, even more unfortunate to be a Chinese woman!

In silk tents and embroidered quilts, everyone has a share in the soul-consuming truth, but once the evil root is planted, I will be pregnant, which is so unsightly, and at the time of childbirth, my liver and intestines will be like a machine. As the ancients said: "A pregnant woman has one foot in the coffin and the other foot outside the coffin." If you are not careful, there is a risk of death, but the cangs can be carefree and lead their lives of picking flowers and dyeing willows. What else in the world is more unfair than this?

This life is over, but the future can be pursued. I only hope that in the next life, I will be reincarnated as a fair and handsome young man, then it will be almost the same, Amitabha!

Returning Home

— Dai Ni

Brief Records of Hometown Life

After eating dinner, we sat in the main room. The kerosene lamp cast large, terrifying shadows across the three sections of the hall. The child slept soundly in my wife's arms, but her hand continued to pat him rhythmically, humming a tune that even she could barely hear. Mother held her water pipe and smoked, replacing each pipeful with a fresh one. Perhaps she also felt the joy of her son, daughter-in-law, and grandchild being reunited at home—a joy deep within her heart, because she never showed a smiling face to anyone else, living so hysterically alone in this dilapidated old house. I sat under the light, reading the day's newspaper. I had never read the newspaper so carefully, especially since I had already glanced through it in the morning. I was conflicted, half clinging to this dilapidated old house, and half thinking about throwing myself into the arms of my second hometown, Shanghai, again at this time tomorrow.

The wind blew across the roof, creating a resonant sound. If it were midnight, one would surely suspect the house was about to collapse. However, I had grown accustomed to it in the last two days, and Mother certainly even more so. Its howling came in gusts and did not attract the attention of any of us, and everything remained silent, except for my wife's humming. The kerosene lamp was suddenly swayed by a gust of wind blowing in through the paper window, and the three large shadows on the wall swayed along with it. My wife yawned, as if speaking to the child, "Let's go to sleep." Everyone seemed to be waiting for these words, stretching or yawning. Mother stood up holding her water pipe and said, "Go to bed early, you have to catch the early train tomorrow." Although she said that, her eyes were fixed on the roof, as if hesitatingly thinking about something; or perhaps it was, "Stay another day before you leave." No matter how bitter enemies were at first, after a long separation, one would somewhat feel the possibility of becoming friends again; moreover, it was ultimately her son in name, and she had also fulfilled her wish to hold a little child. It should be a blessing to be such a wife; but her son, who had not returned for four or five years, was soon to leave again. People are, after all, emotional, especially middle-aged women, and she certainly knew that in the near future she would be an old woman with graying hair. Living alone in this dilapidated old house, could she not recall her days as a girl, the sweet period after her marriage, the sorrow of losing her two sons, and the loneliness of living in this house alone for so many years? Her eyes remained fixed on the roof, perhaps thinking about the past? I stood up sadly and said, "Mom, go to sleep, it's late." I myself didn't understand why I said such a thing, as it was actually earlier than early, the 5:30 PM movie hadn't even ended yet.
